1932.12.08

The League of Nations' Small Nation Representatives Unanimously Endorse the Lytton Report

Firmly Refuse to Recognize the So-Called Puppet State of Manchukuo

But Fail to Explicitly Denounce Japan's Violation of the Covenant

Japanese Side Spreads Rumors of Direct Sino-Japanese Negotiations

(Geneva) The League of Nations Assembly Special Session continued its meeting at 3:40 PM today. Representatives from the four major powers—France, Britain, Italy, and Germany—spoke in succession, none making a clear judgment on right and wrong. However, they advocated for promoting reconciliation between China and Japan based on the Lytton Report. The French representative, Paul-Boncour, argued that the League of Nations should stipulate the general principles for Sino-Japanese negotiations. The British representative, Simon, stated that "We should consider the facts and promote a practical solution, hoping that both the United States and Russia can participate in the Special Committee of Nineteen." The Italian representative, Aloisi, advocated for international cooperation in China's reconstruction and supported Simon's proposal to invite the United States and Russia to participate. According to reporters' observations, the attitude of the major powers is clearly different from that of the small nations, as they are unwilling for the League of Nations to hastily impose sanctions on Japan. (Central News Agency dispatch of the 7th)

(Geneva) The Chinese representative, Quo Tai-chi, is scheduled to deliver a speech at the League of Nations Assembly tomorrow. Small nations are currently campaigning to pass two resolutions: one declaring Japan's violation of the Covenant and the other refusing to recognize Manchukuo. (Central News Agency dispatch of the 7th)

(Geneva) The League of Nations Assembly continued its session at 3:00 PM on the 7th. After the speech by the Uruguayan representative, Borro, representatives from major powers, including the French Foreign Minister, Paul-Boncour, the British Foreign Secretary, Simon, as well as the Dutch representative, Moltesco, the Danish representative, Burbek, the German Foreign Minister, Neurath, and the Turkish representative, Hansupei, spoke in succession. Subsequently, the Chinese Minister to Britain, Quo Tai-chi, and the Japanese representative, Matsuoka, also made supplementary speeches. According to Chairman Hymans, the general debate may be completed tomorrow. (National News Agency dispatch)

(Geneva) Dr. Yen Hui-ching today submitted a telegram from Chiang Kai-shek to the League of Nations Assembly, denying rumors that Chiang supports direct Sino-Japanese negotiations. The Chinese delegation today also submitted a telegram from Su Bingwen to the Assembly, stating that on November 28th, six Japanese aircraft dropped several bombs at the Shiba Li Mu (transliteration) station on the Chinese Eastern Railway, causing casualties among the residents. (Reuters dispatch)

(Geneva) Before the League of Nations Assembly announced the opening of the meeting today (the 7th), the League Secretariat distributed a letter from Japan regarding the resurgence of the anti-Japanese movement in China to all member states. The letter falsely claimed that the anti-Japanese boycott movement had resurged due to the statement by the Chinese representative, Dr. Wellington Koo, at the Executive Yuan meeting, declaring the boycott legitimate. (National News Agency dispatch)

(Geneva) Representatives from various small countries, in their speeches at the General Assembly, expressed sympathy for our country, but failed to explicitly denounce Japan's violation of the Covenant. The Japanese side is still spreading rumors here about impending direct Sino-Japanese negotiations, hoping to confuse international public opinion. (Central News Agency dispatch of the 7th)

The Spanish Representative Speaks from a Legal Standpoint

Japan Disregards International Law and Order

The League of Nations' Procrastination Will Lead to Its Own Demise

(Geneva) The Extraordinary Assembly of the League of Nations convened at 11:00 AM on the 7th. Under the chairmanship of Foreign Minister Hymans, the meeting continued the general discussion on the Sino-Japanese dispute. The Spanish representative, Madariaga, delivered a speech, stating that he acknowledged the complexity and difficulty of the Sino-Japanese dispute, which he described as a conflict between national rationality and international rationality, with the latter potentially having a significant impact on the Japanese people. The Spanish representative praised the League of Nations, saying that it was greatly alarmed when the Manchurian Incident occurred and therefore adopted cautious, wise, and patient actions. He also stated that for every problem, if there is a sincere attempt to resolve it, then the process, even if slow, is acceptable. The task of the Assembly and the League of Nations is to end hostile acts and find a solution to the dispute, as well as to promote all the principles of the League of Nations. Before starting mediation, the League of Nations should first announce its opinion on past events so that mediation can proceed more easily, because a mediation plan must have a foundation and a clear position. Mediation must take into account the interests of the League of Nations; if the League of Nations abandons its responsibilities, it will bring about its own demise. Mediation must also take into account the interests of Japan, because Japan's permanent interests are actually consistent with the interests of the League of Nations. Madariaga also stated that the Spanish government fully accepts the findings and conclusions of the Lytton Commission of Inquiry. The Spanish representative concluded, "The permanent Japan and the historical Japan should learn a lesson from this matter, namely that, at least in terms of method, our opinions are indeed different from those of present-day Japan. What the world needs is order, but order is not about military uniforms or soldiers. The so-called order is none other than rules and legal principles." He also said, "We must uphold legal principles, believe in legal principles, and affirm legal principles." After Madariaga finished speaking, the Chairman invited the Swiss representative, Motta, to speak. (Havas dispatch of the 7th)

The Swiss Representative Speaks from a Moral Perspective

The Swiss representative, Motta, took the floor and was met with thunderous applause. Motta said that he did not wish to openly criticize any of the two major countries involved in the dispute, as Switzerland maintains excellent relations with both. He only wished to speak in defense of the League of Nations Covenant. The Council referred the case to the Assembly in order to allow each member to freely express its views on the dispute and the Lytton Report. The Lytton Report is an excellent document that enhances the prestige of the drafters and the League of Nations. What steps will the League of Nations take after this debate? In his opinion, the Special Committee of Nineteen should propose and supervise a reconciliation procedure. He hoped that this could be achieved, thus avoiding the need to apply Article 15, Paragraph 4 of the Covenant. Was Japan's action a legitimate act of self-defense? The Lytton Report has already provided an unambiguous answer. Did Japan have any intention of military conquest in implementing its expansionist policy? The Lytton Report also has an answer to this. Without Japanese troops, the new state could not be established, but the Inquiry also stated that restoring the status quo is impossible. Motta then referred to the reasons cited by the Japanese for not seeking the League of Nations' assistance, saying that the Japanese reasons contradict Articles 10 and 12. No country should act arbitrarily; this is an essential element for the success of world peace. We have complete sympathy for both countries. We hope for friendly solutions not only on existing disputes, but also on all issues. In short, Japan has overstepped its rights. If Japan accepts the authority of the League of Nations, it will truly enhance its honor and greatly contribute to the strength of morality and the dignity of conscience. (Reuters dispatch)

The Greek Representative Takes the Opportunity to Complain

The Greek representative, Politis, took the floor amidst applause. He said that after listening to the speeches this morning, he did not wish to say much more. The League of Nations had resolved the Shanghai Incident, thereby increasing its prestige. Now there is also the issue of the Three Eastern Provinces awaiting resolution, which is far more difficult than the Shanghai Incident. Fortunately, the Lytton Report has pointed the way forward for this situation, so this book is a tool for finding a final solution. The main issue before the Assembly now is the issue of legitimate self-defense. Self-defense is the right of any country, and immediate plans should be adopted to protect oneself when harmed. As for what the Japanese call legitimate self-defense, from the perspective of international law, the Lytton Report speaks very clearly on this point. If Japan cannot provide evidence to refute it, then the Lytton Report will naturally govern the decision of the Assembly. Politis then recounted an old case from 1925 involving a dispute between Greece and Bulgaria. At that time, Greece accepted the decision of the Council and agreed to pay compensation. Japan in this dispute has indeed been subjected to provocative actions, such as unilateral treaty abrogations and boycotts. But was this danger truly so great that Japan could dispense with seeking the League of Nations' intervention? Although Matsuoka has presented the reasons why Japan did not request the League of Nations to handle the matter, he felt that Japan should at least test the League of Nations' ability to intervene. He did not wish to doubt the sincerity of Japan's will and belief, but he believed that the Assembly's responsibility was to declare the fallacy of Japan's theory. Therefore, there is still hope for the situation, and he believes that the Assembly can still find a basis for friendly resolution and avoid the need to apply Article 15, Paragraph 4. (Reuters)

The representatives of the United States of Central America (Guatemala?) [Note: "中美瓜地瑪拉代表馬都" probably refers to representative of the U.S. of Central America. Guatemala used to be part of a union called United Provinces of Central America or the United States of Central America.] and Madu spoke after Politis, saying that the anxiety of small countries about the Sino-Japanese dispute arises from the principles involved. The government he represents supports the principles contained in the League of Nations Covenant and believes that the Lytton Report should be the basis for all actions of the League of Nations. He is prepared to do his best to support the Lytton Report, and the Guatemalan government advocates for the respect of treaties.

After Madu finished speaking, the Assembly announced the adjournment of the meeting and scheduled a continuation at 3:30 PM this afternoon.

The French Representative, Paul-Boncour's Speech Lacks Clarity

(Geneva) The League of Nations Assembly continued its meeting at 3:40 PM this afternoon. First, the Uruguayan representative, Dr. Borro, spoke, stating that the purpose of his speech was to assist all the powers of the League of Nations and that he supported the establishment of a committee to study ways to find a solution to the dispute.

The French representative, Paul-Boncour, then spoke, saying that the League of Nations is easily criticized. Some believe that its handling of matters is slow and that what applies to the Far East dispute may also apply to future European conflicts. Those who hold this view will realize their mistake in this dispute. The situation is unusual. What we must not forget is that one of the parties in the dispute has the right to station troops in the other country. France, within the League of Nations, is willing to participate in any plan that can restore peace. A year ago, on December 10th, under the chairmanship of Briand, the League of Nations passed a resolution that became the fundamental principle of the Covenant and was attached to a declaration that was not only passed by the Council but also recognized by both parties. Thus, the Inquiry was established, and now its report is being considered. This report is divided into two parts: one for recognition and inspection, and one for conclusions and recommendations. For our benefit, our work should be based on this recognition and recommendations. Before the Assembly, there are two stages: one is conciliation, and on this point, he felt that the smallest basis should be expressed first, so that the conciliation process does not go beyond its scope, and one is that in the future there may be a need to proceed in accordance with Article 15, Paragraph 4. He believed that the report has indicated the best way in which a conciliation procedure can be applied, namely direct discussions between the two parties. The current debate has not yet shown the impressions of both parties regarding the conclusions of the Lytton Report. He believes that it is necessary to have close and detailed discussions on each point separately. This is essential for the initial conciliation procedure. Paul-Boncour's speech lacked clarity and was criticized by many. The British Foreign Secretary, Simon, spoke after Paul-Boncour. The text repeatedly mentioned Article 15, Paragraph 4 of the Covenant, the original text of which is recorded below: If the dispute cannot be resolved in this way, the Council, by a vote of all or a majority, shall issue a report stating the facts of the dispute and the recommendations that the Council deems appropriate.

The Situation of the Meeting the Day Before Yesterday

(Geneva) The Special Assembly of the League of Nations continued its meeting at 3:45 PM on the afternoon of the 6th. The representatives of Ireland, Connolly, Sweden, Eden, and the Czech Foreign Minister, Benes, successively expressed their views as follows:

The South Irish Representative Cries Out Loudly That If the League of Nations Is Timid and Does Not Move Forward, Itself Will Have No Way to Survive

(Geneva) When the League of Nations Assembly continued its meeting this afternoon, the Irish representative, Connolly, first spoke, saying that the Lytton Report and the actions that the Assembly can take in this regard not only relate to China and Japan but also to the future of the League of Nations itself. The major issue of war and peace in the Far East and its inevitable impact on world peace are all closely linked to the resolution of the report. He said this not to exaggerate; the Assembly must make a fair judgment based on the facts and seek a solution that is equal to all parties concerned in order to eliminate this conflict and the possibility of future enmity. Many critics believe that the League of Nations is incapable of handling major issues. He and many people in Ireland also held this view, but since he arrived in Geneva, he has begun to feel that the League of Nations has the utmost power to maintain world peace in its constitution. However, the League of Nations must be prepared to earnestly and bravely safeguard the League of Nations Covenant and its own decisions. If it retreats or is apprehensive and concerned about offending people, then the League of Nations cannot survive and is not worth surviving. The Lytton Report has found several signs that the Assembly should pay attention to. The most obvious is that the report seems to have indicated that Japan, in order to seek its own interests, is using imperialist expansion methods and completely disregards the infringement of the territorial rights of another sovereign state. What is undeniable is that the activities of Japan in establishing and maintaining "Manchukuo" cannot be ignored. The concerns of the world that Japanese officials will eventually completely manage "Manchukuo" are not without reason. The report has clearly stated that Japan has indeed committed actions that violate the League of Nations Covenant, the Kellogg-Briand Pact, and the Nine-Power Treaty. Due to these violations, "Manchukuo" has been established. Among the conclusions of the Lytton Report, it is said that restoring the status quo will not solve the problem, and maintaining and recognizing "Manchukuo" is not a satisfactory solution because it disregards the wishes of the people of Manchuria and it is doubtful whether it will benefit Japan's ultimate interests. In his view, this section is the key point of the situation, and the phrase "whether it will benefit Japan's ultimate interests" is particularly important. Japan's real interests in Manchuria are acknowledged and must be given due consideration. However, protecting these interests by peaceful means is more solid than using force. He hoped that the Assembly would agree with him, and he hoped that Japan, after thinking about it, would also agree. Now that the Lytton Report is placed before us, if we are not prepared to deny the conclusions, the countries attending this meeting must declare their refusal to recognize "Manchukuo." If we want to maintain the integrity of the League of Nations, he sees no other way to do it. Japan may say that Japan has sacrificed lives and money to consolidate its position in Manchuria. However, in the world's "wars to end all wars," millions of lives have been lost and billions of dollars have been spent, and the only result is that the world is confused and disoriented and is in a state of social and economic turmoil. The League of Nations was born out of this war, and what it maintains in the world depends only on a thread of treaty. We must not allow anyone to cut this thread. What small countries pay the most attention to is that the principles of the League of Nations Covenant must be firmly maintained. If the moral strength of the League of Nations is broken on this point, how can the existing League of Nations survive? The Lytton Report expresses the idea that the establishment of a local police force in Manchuria may be the basis for a final solution. This point can also be noted. Japan must know that if it insists on its current attitude, it will cause Japan to be despised. If Japan refuses to comply with the conditions of the League of Nations Covenant, it will lose goodwill and commercial relations. However, the responsibility of the League of Nations Assembly to maintain the method of applying the Covenant at any cost does not diminish because of this. If the Japanese people find it difficult to understand this view, it is truly a pity. The Irish Free State is extremely opposed to the idea of imperialist expansion. He felt that the Assembly should earnestly accept the Lytton Report. He, on behalf of the South Irish government, accepts it without hesitation. As far as the Irish Free State is concerned, it will adopt the recommendations of the Lytton Commission of Inquiry and refuse to recognize any new country established in Manchuria in its current state. Now that South Ireland has made this declaration in earnest, it is also willing to contribute its possible assistance to seek a solution based on the Lytton Report.

The Czech Foreign Minister Speaks Eloquently

Sincerely Uphold the Dignity of the League of Nations Covenant

Maintain Peace and Forbid Lenience Towards Japan

The Czech Foreign Minister, Dr. Benes, then spoke, mentioning the importance of this issue, saying that since the establishment of the League of Nations, the Assembly has been convened to act under Article 15 of the Covenant. This is the first time that a final and effective solution to the issue or a measure involving arbitration may be involved. This issue concerns the whole world, the area involved is larger than the combined area of France and Germany, and the country involved has more people than the total number of residents elsewhere on the planet, and in political, economic, and spiritual terms, it involves the other two major countries which are not members of the League of Nations. What the Czech Republic is concerned about is purely a matter of principle, because the Czech Republic wishes to maintain the most friendly relations with both parties to this case. He did not wish to rush to a judgment on this conflict. There are things that must be determined first: Has the obligation of the Covenant been violated? Have the obligations of the various international conventions been respected by both parties? Have the resolutions of the Council and the Assembly been observed by both parties? Has the League of Nations handled this issue with a non-hasty or impartial attitude, or with the spirit of perseverance and justice? This is the most important issue for the League of Nations, because it will set a precedent. He has said a lot about the issue of principle. Now please allow him to speak about the issue of fact. He advocates passing the Lytton Report. This book is a valuable, solemn, and very fair document. The report has stated that Japan's military actions in Manchuria and Shanghai cannot be recognized as acts of legitimate self-defense. This directly states that the land of a member of the League of Nations has been invaded by Japan. In this case, no other conclusion is possible, unless the League of Nations Covenant has not been respected by Japan. There is also a situation where if there is a question of legitimate self-defense, it must be based on the other party's misconduct. Based on the Lytton Report and the documents submitted by both parties, there are two types of behaviors that may be of this nature: one is the boycott propaganda, which even extends to schools, and the other is the organized, systematic, and seemingly promoted by the authorities anti-Japanese boycott movement. This type of behavior is of course reprehensible, but if a member state of the League of Nations arbitrarily carries out large-scale military actions on the land of another member state, then the League of Nations must take firm action. In the final resolution, the allegations regarding anti-foreignism and anti-boycott should be given serious consideration. The Czech representative mentioned the issue of the creation of "Manchukuo", saying that this also involves issues of principle, etc., and is more serious. Within the land of a member state of the League of Nations, an independent country is established due to the presence of the military of another member state. May I ask if this is not a clear violation of Article 10 of the League of Nations Covenant? Is this not a very dangerous precedent? What would you think if the same situation occurred in Europe? Preventing the establishment of a precedent is critical. If other countries follow suit, the consequences will be unimaginable. As a guarantor of respect for treaties, if a country does not respect the Nine-Power Treaty, is the League of Nations not concerned about it? What must be acknowledged now is that the responsibility for not complying with certain treaty obligations is now also placed on other parties. The Special Committee of Nineteen has expressed its regret that the commitment by both parties not to aggravate the situation has not been fulfilled. What is even more disappointing to the Special Committee is that Japan's recognition of "Manchukuo" has made the mediation work extremely difficult. Particularly serious actions that are contrary to the League of Nations Covenant and the provisions of the Assembly resolutions have occurred. This unfair behavior must be justified. In any case, the League of Nations cannot recognize it. This is obvious regarding the resolution of March 11th of this year. Before we begin to proceed based on Article 15, Paragraph 4 of the Covenant, please do not create a situation that forces us to act as judges. Japan has a glorious history and occupies a position among the world's first-class countries. China has an ancient civilization and is the source of the progressive aspirations of today's emerging countries. We ask these two countries to seek a solution to their conflict through sincere, faithful, and friendly mediation. Even if this effort fails despite our assistance, the League of Nations' work will then be to adjudicate. The League of Nations must have the courage to act without reservation or hesitation, firmly and solemnly, and in accordance with the public interest. The Assembly cannot take ambiguous actions on issues involving principles. Even if it cannot obtain an immediate and effective solution, there should be no doubt about the Assembly's firm will.

The Swedish Representative Speaks Candidly

Firmly Uphold the Lytton Report

Severely Denounce Japan's Support for the Puppet State of Manchukuo

The Swedish representative, Eden, then spoke, saying that the current relationship between China and Japan is actually a disguised war. All actions that do not respect treaties will cause major disputes in international relations. International constraints must never be disregarded by the selfish actions of any single country. This approach can never be recognized. The responsibility of the Assembly is to decide whether the violation of the treaty is a legitimate act of self-defense. The Lytton Report already has a clear answer to this. The Japanese side said that the situation in Manchuria has changed due to the establishment of the new independent "Manchukuo." However, the Lytton Report said that the establishment of the new state was due to the Japanese military's occupation of the Three Eastern Provinces. The Assembly should base its arguments on the Lytton Report when passing resolutions. When the Assembly passed a resolution on March 3 of this year, the Assembly stated that the actions of the Japanese military in the Three Eastern Provinces had indeed infringed on the territorial integrity of another member of the League of Nations. Therefore, recognizing "Manchukuo" is an act that violates Article 10 of the Covenant. If negotiations to resolve the dispute are to be conducted at this time, the situation is very inappropriate. Since the League of Nations cannot order the troops of one party to withdraw from the territory of the other party, all negotiations will be conducted under military pressure. This is contrary to the spirit of the Covenant. The current situation is extremely dangerous, so the Assembly should not suspend discussions before deciding on a solution.

The Norwegian Representative Speaks Righteously

Opposes Any Kind of Militarism

China and Japan Should Be Peacefully Mediated

Afterwards, the Norwegian representative, Lange, stood up and spoke, first saying that the Assembly had allowed the extension of the period for discussion to be extended due to special circumstances. He then praised the Lytton Commission of Inquiry, saying that the Lytton Report was extremely fair and that the best way for the Assembly to resolve the Sino-Japanese dispute was to adopt the Lytton Report's proposals. He also stated that he was absolutely opposed to any country acting arbitrarily and disregarding everything. Lange then continued, saying that historically, there have been many cases of land being seized by force, but now there is the existence of the League of Nations Covenant and other arbitration treaties, so there are better methods of mediation than military occupation. He also mentioned the resolution of March 11 and said that he hoped that China and Japan could work hard to find a method of mediation with the assistance of all member states of the League of Nations, and that all countries with interests in the Far East would be willing to participate and work together with the League of Nations, and that this effort would not only be limited to expressing opinions and interpreting treaties but would also seek to achieve the purpose of resolving the issue. China and Japan are actually interdependent. Japan may have grievances, but a way to mediate the interests of both parties in the Three Eastern Provinces cannot fail to be found.

The Assembly adjourned at 5:55 PM. The next meeting is scheduled for Wednesday morning at 10:45 AM, at which time representatives from Spain, Switzerland, and Greece will speak. (Reuters dispatch of the 6th)

Lord Lytton's Speech at a London Banquet

Hoping Japan Will Not Take Actions to Undermine the League of Nations

(London) Tonight, the League of Nations Society held a banquet, attended by personnel from both the Chinese and Japanese embassies. Lord Lytton, in an impromptu speech, stated that the current situation is no longer merely an abstract or legal issue, but rather concerns the actions of individuals. It is now understood that the underlying issue is always one of people. When asked if there was any hope for a resolution, Lytton replied that his initial impression of last week's League of Nations Council meeting was that there was little progress. However, he later realized that the Council meeting was not a waste of time. If both parties in the Council meeting had expressed their acceptance of the report and were willing to use it as a starting point for new negotiations, the Council would have welcomed such a statement and forwarded the report to the Assembly with a proposal to begin negotiations immediately. Although this was not the case, there was still cause for comfort. Thus, the Assembly held its meeting in a spirit of hope. The League of Nations only asks two things of Japan: first, that Japan has full confidence in the League and is certain that it will not be forced to abandon any interests it considers vital; and second, that Japan expresses its willingness to ensure that its vital interests do not conflict with the equally important interests of other countries. Some believe that a solution can be achieved simply with Japan's agreement, but in fact, China's agreement is also necessary. Neither side desires our praise or criticism, but rather to be understood and trusted by us. (Reuters, 6th)

Chairman Lord Cecil spoke, discussing the League of Nations Assembly, saying he hoped the solution determined by the Assembly would conform to the principles of law and fairness that the League upholds among its member states. As for each country's right to judge its own disputes, that is completely inapplicable to civilized international life today. (National Telegram, 6th)

Current Commentary

After the Opening of the League of Nations Assembly: Prospects Dim

1. China's Hope

Since the September 18th Incident, our government has exercised restraint and caution, prioritizing the maintenance of peace and avoiding the reckless initiation of hostilities. Therefore, even though three northeastern provinces have been lost, our people have responded to the opponent's aggression with only peaceful and temperate resistance. At the same time, we have placed full trust in the League of Nations, even though its resolutions have been trampled upon time and again. The League of Nations Covenant, the Washington Nine-Power Treaty, and the Kellogg-Briand Pact have all been torn apart by Japan's iron fist. "Public justice" and "righteousness" have all been reduced to mud under the iron hooves of militarism. The 3,776,700 square miles of land in the three northeastern provinces have been ravaged, and more than 30,080,000 people have become prisoners of the Japanese. Although our entire nation is filled with "indignation and hatred towards the enemy," we remain courteous and respectful. Therefore, since Japan launched its unprovoked military campaign, our country has not severed diplomatic relations with Japan, and envoys continue to travel back and forth as before. This clearly demonstrates the sincerity of our government and people in upholding peace and trusting the League of Nations.

With the opening of the special session of the League of Nations Assembly on the 6th of this month, our representatives will once again exert their eloquence to negotiate among the nations, hoping for the revival of public justice and righteousness. Furthermore, we hope that the League of Nations can uphold its original intention in establishing the League and, for the sake of bolstering the League's prestige, make an impartial judgment. If mediation has failed and conciliation is in vain, and if the Japanese military aggression continues unabated, not only will our country suffer losses, but world peace will also be adversely affected. Now that the entire case has been transferred to the Assembly for resolution, the only option is to immediately apply the provisions of Article 16 of the Covenant. The member states of the League of Nations should "immediately sever all commercial or financial relations with (Japan, which is engaging in warfare) and prevent all intercourse between their nationals and the nationals of the covenant-breaking State." More importantly, "the Council of the League shall recommend to the several Governments concerned what effective military, naval or air force the Members of the League shall severally contribute to the armed forces to be used to protect the covenants of the League." Otherwise, the last opportunity to test the credibility of the League of Nations will be lost forever.

2. Japan's Strategy

From the beginning of its invasion of the Northeast, Japan's underlying intention was to seize our country's territory. Therefore, it blatantly claimed that "China is not a modern and organized state" in order to arbitrarily divide it. In the diplomatic arena, it constantly hinted that it was assuming the first line of defense against Russia in the Far East and touted the high-sounding slogan of "Open Door in Manchuria." At the same time, it eagerly sought to cozy up to the Soviet Union, adding to the fisheries agreement and the petroleum agreement, and ordered Hirota (former ambassador to the Soviet Union) to return to Japan to carefully devise a plan. Matsuoka went to Moscow to carefully examine the Soviet Union's true intentions, believing that if a genuine understanding could be established between Japan and the Soviet Union, then Japan's annexation of the three northeastern provinces would not become a problem. However, the Soviet Union remained cautiously observant and would not be fooled by Japan. Before launching the Mukden Incident, Japan had made various preparations and claimed to have a tacit understanding with France. Japan did not fully trust the experienced and prudent British, but wanted to enlist France as its ally. However, with the recent signing of the Franco-Soviet Non-Aggression Pact and the resurgence of the American war debt issue, France, in order to maintain its hegemony in Europe, had eased its conflicts with the Soviet Union and was facing a renewed tension in its relations with Germany and Italy. Therefore, it had to seek understanding from the United States, and its support for Japan had to fade. With Japan and the United States being mutually incompatible, and its relationship with the Soviet Union being only temporary, Japan's pursuit remained focused on France. Recently, it even openly signaled that if France could assist Japan in the League of Nations Assembly by supporting its demand to recognize "Manchuria as a fait accompli" and promoting direct negotiations between China and Japan, Japan would do its utmost to support France's proposed new arms reduction plan to ensure France's "security." Furthermore, it could assist France in its state-owned enterprises advancing northward from Annam. However, what will actually happen will depend on the direction the world takes. However, France is too far from the Far East, its interests are minimal, and it cannot obtain the benefits of the Chinese Eastern Railway as desired. Therefore, its goodwill towards Japan may be limited to mere formalities.

3. The Outcome of the League of Nations Assembly

Although our country strongly upholds justice, unfortunately, its strength is too weak to support justice with force. As a result, Japan's arrogance has increased. The League of Nations, in this situation, should not favor Japan simply because our strength is weak. However, how to make Japan submit is the current question. The League of Nations is currently busy with disarmament and mending the rifts in Europe, and it is difficult to attend to the Far Eastern problem and lacks the power to enforce its will. Moreover, it fears Japan's firm opposition. Therefore, as for how the League of Nations Assembly will handle the Northeast issue in the future, I believe that there are three possible scenarios:

First, the member states of the League of Nations (especially the smaller countries) are all aware of Japan's conspiracy and believe that it must be restrained. Therefore, they advocate for the formation of a powerful mediation committee that includes the United States and the Soviet Union to compel Japan to submit.

Second, no resolution is made for the time being, and the "Manchukuo (puppet) state" is not recognized. Instead, the situation will be observed and allowed to develop. This is because discerning people in various countries believe that Japan cannot occupy the Northeast for long and will fall into difficulties due to financial collapse, eventually returning to the framework of the League of Nations.

Third, the League of Nations serves as a mediator to facilitate direct negotiations between China and Japan to restore the balance of power in the Far East.

Of the above three, the first and third are strongly opposed by Japan, and the chances of their realization are probably slim. Will "delaying" and "observing" be the trend of the future?

Mingcheng Gained and Lost Again

The National Consultative Assembly Regulations Have Not Yet Been Drafted

Drafting Committee Members Disagree

Whether to Submit to the Third Plenary Session for Discussion Is Undecided

(Nanjing) The National Consultative Assembly was originally named the National Representative Assembly, which was approved by the Luoyang National Crisis Conference. After detailed review by the Central Government, the name was changed to the National Consultative Assembly. Chen Guofu, Gu Mengyu, Chen Gongbo, Zhu Jiahua, Duan Xipeng, Luo Jialun, Zhang Daofan, Tang Youren, Ye Chucang, and other nine people were appointed as members of the regulations drafting committee. Before Wang left the country, he also participated in the discussion of this meeting. Several meetings have been held, but the opinions of all parties have been inconsistent, and the matter has been delayed until now. It is heard that the opinions of the drafting members have recently been summarized as follows: 1. The national representatives of the National Consultative Assembly will be produced by popular elections in each province, selecting three times the number of representatives. From these three times the number of candidates, the Central Government will then designate the representatives. 2. The powers of the Consultative Assembly. In the early stages of democratic politics, civil rights are not yet fully realized. The Central Government should first implement a flexible measure to promote civil rights, namely, to expand the nature of the Central Political Council and form it into a Senate like those in European and American countries. This will make the nature of the National Consultative Assembly resemble the House of Representatives in European and American countries. In this way, in the initial period of the Consultative Assembly, the final decision on all political programs will temporarily remain with the Central Political Council, which is the political center. The main point of the failure to pass the organizational regulations is that the boundary between the assembly and the Central Government cannot be clarified. Because the Consultative Assembly is the initial implementation of democratic politics, its responsibility should be to represent the people and offer opinions to the Central Government in principle. All issues that are closely related to the functions and powers of the Central National Government, which the Central Government itself cannot resolve, may be discussed and decided by the Consultative Assembly. Conversely, the Central Political Council may also decide. The significance of this point is that some people argue that the responsibility of the Consultative Assembly is limited to offering opinions to the Central Government. The above points have not yet been fully determined by all parties. It is still difficult to predict whether the case will be submitted to the Third Plenary Session and, if so, whether it will be included in the agenda. (Special Dispatch, 7th)

Yangtze River Hydropower Plant Site Determined

(Nanjing) The site of the Yangtze River Hydropower Plant is currently being surveyed by Zhao Ruizhi, a hydropower expert from the Construction Commission, S. Elstrup, chief engineer of the Yangtze River Conservancy Commission, Song Xishang, director of the Public Works Department, and other technical personnel in Sichuan. Yesterday, Song said that the survey results indicated that two locations, one 45 miles east of Yichang and the other 20 miles above Yichang, are the most suitable, as they have average water flow strength and are located on plains, facilitating industrial development. The designed power plant has a generating capacity of 320,000 kilowatts. Due to considerations for transportation and flooding, the project is relatively large and will require more than ten million yuan and three years to complete. All detailed plans and charts are currently being expedited by the Yangtze River Conservancy Commission and will be submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval in one month. (7th Dispatch)

The Ministry of Foreign Affairs Lodges a Strong Protest Against the Japanese Army's Massacre of Farmers in Fushun

The Japanese Government Actually Sends a Note to Our Ministry of Foreign Affairs Denying It

(Nanjing) Regarding the case of the Japanese army luring villagers, men, women, old, and young, in Pingdingshan, Qianjinzai, Lizigou, and other places in Fushun and mowing them down with machine guns, resulting in the tragic death of over 2,700 people, the Japanese government actually sent a note to our Ministry of Foreign Affairs denying it after our side announced it. They also regarded the news published in the Shanghai News as damaging the "reputation of the Imperial Army" and demanded a ban. It is heard that the government has already investigated the aforementioned massacre and has complete and conclusive evidence, recognizing that this kind of action is truly inhumane and has attracted the attention of the world. On the 6th, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs specially responded to the Japanese ambassador, not only refuting the note but also lodging a strong protest. The general meaning is as follows: The evidence in this case is conclusive and cannot be denied with empty words. The Japanese army has illegally occupied the three northeastern provinces for more than a year, and there has hardly been a day without incidents of killing, abusing, and oppressing people in that area. Countless of our people have died tragically or been injured by Japanese guns, cannons, aircraft, and bombs, and the loss of property they have suffered is also unprecedented. At the beginning of this year, the Japanese army, navy, and air force dared to arbitrarily attack Chinese residents with the latest weapons in Shanghai, a center of international commerce in China, resulting in countless deaths and injuries, and setting fire to houses and prohibiting extinguishing them. Their cruelty and ruthlessness have reached this point. Now, the Japanese army has wantonly massacred more than 2,700 Chinese farmers in Pingdingshan and other villages near Fushun, without sparing even women and children. This is truly a rare occurrence in human history. Not only are the Chinese people extremely angry, but people all over the world are also shocked by it. Regarding the so-called "damage to the reputation of the Imperial Army," the Ministry of Foreign Affairs responded in the note that the Chinese government believes that the best way for the Japanese government to maintain the reputation of the Japanese army is to initially prevent the Japanese army from illegally occupying the three northeastern provinces and attacking Shanghai, and not to order the killing of people. Now, it should quickly withdraw all the Japanese troops illegally occupying the eastern provinces. However, the Japanese government does not do this, and often distorts the facts or denies the facts after the Japanese army carries out aggression by force. In reality, it is only sufficient to expose the responsibilities that the Japanese government should bear. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs stated at the end of the note that the evidence for the Japanese army's massacre of farmers in villages near Fushun is conclusive, as mentioned above, and it is difficult to tolerate the attempt to deny it with empty words. In addition to reserving all rights regarding this case, a strong protest is hereby lodged. (7th Central News Agency Dispatch)

President Hoover's Policy Report to Joint Session of U.S. Congress

War Debt Issue Under Negotiation with Debtor Nations; U.S. Banking System Must Be Greatly Reformed

International Cooperation to Solve Economic Problems

▲ The National News Agency, Washington, 7th - Today, the U.S. Congress specially convened a joint session of the Senate and House of Representatives to listen to President Hoover read out his annual policy report. The content mainly focused on domestic issues. Regarding war debts, the description was quite brief, only stating that the government is currently engaged in negotiations with debtor nations, and will make a special report to Congress once the negotiations are completed. However, his wording was quite capable of making members of Congress feel that they could not take this matter lightly.

World Economic Conference

He spoke quite earnestly about the domestic and international economic situation, guaranteeing that after the World Economic Conference is successful, it will be possible to raise prices. Therefore, he earnestly urged international cooperation to solve economic problems, stating that the welfare of our people is tied to the peace of the world, the disarmament of the world, and the recovery of the world economy. However, these problems can only be solved if each party has sincere friendship, abides by the agreements it has made, until they are mutually revised, and then adds international cooperation, determined to seek mutually beneficial solutions. We are preparing to hold a World Economic Conference, which, if successful, will greatly increase the prices of agricultural products, promote industry and commerce, and reduce unemployment. We are actively engaged in the World Disarmament Conference, which, if successful, will reduce the burden of taxation, increase political stability, and reduce the risk of war because it will increase the defense capabilities of various countries and reduce the aggressive capabilities of various countries.

Financial Revenue and Expenditure

As for domestic affairs, he also advocated adopting a universal sales tax, greatly reducing salaries, improving banking laws, and reducing services for veterans, declaring that the budget for the coming year must seek a balance between revenue and expenditure. The way to increase revenue is to expand the scope of taxation. In practice, a sales tax should be levied on all manufactured goods, but this tax must be levied uniformly, and only food and certain clothing can be exempted. However, most members of both houses of Congress seemed to pay little attention to the president's proposal for a sales tax. Next, he discussed the issue of salary reductions, saying that the 500 million yuan saved in last year's budget was because the economy was declining and the people's livelihood was declining. The government had to increase services to the public, resulting in many unexpected expenses, which consumed most of what was originally intended to be saved last year. However, at a time when public and private finances are in trouble, the government must strive to be thrifty. He has drafted a salary reduction plan that can generally be reduced by about 15%. He also said that at the end of an economic downturn, the people are greatly hit, and in the future, they must seek to provide the people with appropriate guarantees to avoid further...

Reform the Banking System

There was a fear of shocking the people. The United States was not prepared for the arrival of this economic downturn, and its banking system was not sufficient to cope with the crisis, resulting in successive bankruptcies and shocking the public, which was a major cause of deep pain. The number of bank failures in the United States in the past year accounted for 10.5% of the total. In contrast, no bank failed in the United Kingdom, which shows that the U.S. banking system is flawed and needs to be greatly reformed by Congress. He also said that the previous Congress authorized the president to reorganize various administrative agencies, and a plan for the merger and consolidation has now been drafted, which will be announced by administrative order in a few days. It is estimated that more than 50 places will be merged and consolidated. If Congress does not express its disapproval within 60 days, it will be enacted as law.

In this presidential report, there was no special plan for economic relief. Some congressional leaders expressed disappointment, but the president believed that the economy is currently on a path to recovery, and the government's main task is to pay attention to it at all times and not allow it to be hindered.

Hunger-Stricken People Petition in an Orderly Manner

Reuters, Washington, 6th - Three thousand hunger marchers, led by a band playing revolutionary music, marched through the streets today to present petitions to the speakers of the Senate and House of Representatives, demanding immediate allocation of cash for relief and the implementation of unemployment insurance. As the Anglo-French Paris Conference Approaches, War Debts Will Be Paid Soon; France Fears Political Upheaval as a Result

Reuters, Paris, 7th - British Prime Minister MacDonald and French Prime Minister Herriot both arrived here from Geneva this morning. As for whether Britain and France will pay the war debts due on December 15th, MacDonald and Herriot do not seem to have made a final decision. British Chancellor of the Exchequer Chamberlain is also expected to arrive here tonight. After the three politicians consult tomorrow, they will definitely have a resolution on this matter. According to reliable sources, if Britain decides to pay as expected, then France will take the same attitude. If so, the French parliament is feared to overthrow the government because of opposition to paying the money, and then the prime minister will likely still be Herriot. The two prime ministers did not meet today; tomorrow will be a very important day.

Reuters, London, 7th - The hope that the U.S. might not insist on the payment of the December installment of debts is now gradually dispelled by President Hoover's message to Congress. British and French political figures are therefore meeting in Paris tonight to discuss the current situation in the context of the "Gentleman's Agreement" reached in Lausanne. From a legal point of view, the payment of the December installment of debts cannot be regarded as a failure to reach a satisfactory settlement with the U.S. Payment is a necessary event before adjudication, so the Lausanne Agreement issue does not arise at present. Although Britain can decide to pay in full, France, even if it can pay, will suspend remittance temporarily. The French prime minister may get a small majority in parliament on this policy. It is heard that disarmament will also be discussed in Paris. It is expected that the discussion will be completed by Thursday, at which time the British Prime Minister will return to Geneva, and the French Prime Minister will also go to Geneva a little later.

Reuters, Washington, 6th - The Czech government is now warning the U.S. that if the deadline for suspending war debt payments cannot be extended, there will be adverse consequences, and U.S. trade with the Czech Republic will be affected. If the Czech Republic pays the war debts due on December 15th, it will endanger the structure of its existing economy and finances. The Czech Republic's second reply has now been sent to Secretary of State Stimson.

Havas, Brussels, 6th - Belgium's reply to the U.S. was telegraphed out yesterday, explaining the important issues of Belgium's position in the war debt issue, the circumstances of the war debt loan, the situation created by the Hoover moratorium plan, and Germany's failure to pay reparations.

Japanese Mine Torpedoes a Japanese Merchant Ship

Regarding the disaster of the "Sawarabi", the Ministry of the Navy released the following statement yesterday: The cause of the "Sawarabi" disaster has been reported previously. Proposals for the Third Plenary Session Have Been Sorted Out, and the Report on Bandit Suppression is Also Completed

Hankou Correspondence: Chairman Chiang has been in Hankou supervising the suppression of remaining bandits from summer to winter, for seven months. Now, with the Third Plenary Session about to convene, he has decided to go to Nanjing to attend. All proposals have been sorted out, and the report on bandit suppression was completed on the 6th. The content mainly includes the progress of bandit suppression, political reforms, road construction, and local rehabilitation, all comprehensively collected, compiled by responsible drafters, and submitted to Secretary-General Yang Yongtai for review and printing in preparation for Chiang to take to Nanjing to report to the meeting. According to Chiang's report at the expanded memorial week at the headquarters on the 5th, the date of departure will be soon. However, according to a certain source, Chiang has decided to depart on the 8th and is expected to arrive in Nanjing on the 10th. The trip to Jiangxi cannot be realized temporarily due to the urgency of time. Recently, Chiang has been making extraordinary efforts in political reforms. As expressed at the memorial week on the 5th, he has devoted himself to military affairs for the first three months since July and to politics for the following four months, which is no exaggeration. He regards rural relief and education reform as particularly urgent. Regarding the rural relief issue, a relief office has been established, and one million yuan has been allocated for revolving finance. Various regulations have been promulgated to complete the Baojia organization within the specified time limit and to quickly establish rural cooperative preparatory societies to receive loans and lend to poor farmers, in order to implement this policy. The office has been working tirelessly under Chiang's orders, sending important officials such as Liu Ruxiang and Ling Jingshan to conduct on-site inspections in rural areas of various counties, and instructing the county magistrates to pay attention to seven matters: (1) Strictly follow the progress schedule issued by the headquarters for completing the Baojia organization, with the final deadline for the third phase set for January 5, 1933, to complete all tasks and submit a detailed report on the general situation of the countryside within ten days. (2) Rural residents who are truly unable to resume their businesses must meet the conditions stipulated in the articles of association of the rural cooperative preparatory societies in the bandit suppression areas in order to join the society. Attention must be paid to prevent them from being members of more than two societies at the same time, leading to opportunism. (3) The Agricultural Rehabilitation Committee should be established immediately. (4) Before the establishment of the cooperative preparatory societies, it is feared that farmers' knowledge is immature and the organization cannot be sound. Widespread publicity should be carried out to make it known to every household. The guidance, registration, loan application, and lending should be supervised, and the roster of members should be submitted. (5) The needed cattle, seeds, agricultural tools, and other necessities for rural areas may be requested from ? for planning before the preparatory societies are established. (6) Members of the preparatory societies should bear joint and several liability according to the regulations. Those who do not have the ability to live independently should not be allowed to ? arbitrarily, causing abuses. (7) Local tyrants and evil gentry are the pests of the countryside. In the emergency relief of the bandit areas, it is necessary to strictly prevent such ? from mixing in. Regarding the urgent relief of rural areas in the bandit areas, several consultations have been held with Xu Shiying, who returned to Shanghai on the evening of the 6th to raise relief funds. Regarding the issue of education reform, in addition to curbing the education unrest and ordering all suspended schools to resume classes, it was also decided to hold a speech at the Chonghua Cinema (designated as the Pacification Commissioner's Office) at 10 AM on the 7th, gathering principals, teachers, and five representatives from each class of middle schools in Hankou, as well as all members of the General Chamber of Commerce. In the afternoon, they crossed the river to gather middle school students and above in Wuchang for a speech. It was also decided to inspect the boy scouts of various schools in Wuhan at Zhongshan Park on the morning of the 8th, and to send Zhong Han, director of the Political Training Department of the headquarters, to handle military education in various schools in Henan, Hubei, and Anhui provinces for rectification. Resolution of the Bengbu Salt Dispute

After Mediation by Officials and Gentry, Both Salt Merchants and Salt Firms Made Concessions, and the North Salt Public Business Office and Salt Firms Resumed Business as Usual

Bengbu Correspondence: Previously, the local salt industry had a dispute with salt merchants over the objection to the North Salt Public Business Office, and the two sides were at odds for more than a month. Salt merchants were constrained by the salt firms and could not trade, and salt ? could not sell salt due to the lack of intermediaries, causing significant losses to both sides, and both were financially exhausted, making it difficult to continue. Xu Tingyao, commander of the Fourth Division stationed in Bengbu and commander of the garrison, believed that the salt industry was related to the people's livelihood, and if the delay was not resolved for a long time, it would have a great impact on the market. He specially invited local gentry Gao Weixuan, Peng Zhuoru,

Li Peisheng, and others to come forward to mediate and persuade both parties to make concessions to each other. After one mediation, both salt firms and salt merchants expressed their acceptance. On the 4th, he invited the backbones of the salt firms and salt merchants to meet and earnestly discuss and decide on the following compromise measures: (1)

The North Salt Public Business Office and all salt firms will resume business as usual. (2) All merchants who purchase salt must have the salt firms appraise the price and see the salt samples at the Salt Industry Association before paying the money to sell salt through the North Salt Public Business Office. (3) Each stone of salt will be charged a commission of 1 dime and 2 cents by the salt firms, plus 2 dimes and 4 cents for public security levy, school levy, and public association levy, for a total of 1 dime and 4 cents and 4 cents. The salt firms will receive 5 cents and 4 cents less than before. (4) The salt firms must stamp the salt when it is unloaded. (5) The money owed by the salt firms to the salt merchants will be repaid by Gao Weixuan and others within seven days, and the debtors will be responsible for the repayment. After the above measures were approved by both parties, they resumed business as usual on the 5th. Xiang Yuncheng, chairman of the Salt Industry Association, specially convened representatives of the salt ? at the association in the afternoon to report on the mediation process. All salt firm owners and partners expressed their satisfaction because the salt firms still operated as usual, and their livelihoods would not be panicked. The salt industry dispute that had lasted for more than a month was completely resolved (November 6th).

The maintenance association was obviously organized under the order of the Japanese army. He said that he had registered with the Municipal Public Security Bureau when he organized the association. This prosecutor believes that there is no need to investigate this point because the matter ? is handled on behalf of the enemy, and even if it is registered, it is a crime. As long as the goods passed through the occupied area of the Japanese army, they could pass when they saw the pass signed by him. If he did not collude with the Japanese army, why would the Japanese army release the goods when they saw the pass signed by him? As for the part of the pistol, it is now ? found that the section of the indictment on privately hiding a pistol should be abandoned.

The Inside Story of the Taiyuan Student Movement

Recently, several schools in Taiyuan City suddenly experienced an unusually intense student movement. Students of Shanxi University demanded living expenses from the president, Wang Lu. Wang was unable to meet the demands and therefore expressed his resignation. At the same time, students from normal schools and junior high schools throughout the city have been petitioning the Education Department and the provincial government for days, demanding the restoration of the government-funded system, because the authorities cancelled subsidies and collected tuition fees this year, making it difficult for them to study. In addition, students at the Provincial No. 1 Middle School discovered the expulsion of the principal, Cui Xuanyan, and the Provincial Normal School also experienced infighting over the expulsion of the principal, Huang Quan, with students divided into "supporting Huang" and "expelling Huang" factions. Several people in the expelling Huang faction were severely beaten. For several days (from November 23 to November 27), students from provincial and government-funded schools [Shanxi University, No. 1 Middle School, No. 1 Normal School, No. 1 Women's Normal School, etc.] gathered at the Education Department to voice their grievances, petition the provincial government, and stage demonstrations. Posters and declarations were plastered all over the city, and the streets were filled with them, creating a situation like a prairie fire. The causes of this student movement, on the surface, seem to be nothing more than the decline of Shanxi currency, the bankruptcy of the rural economy, the hardship of people's livelihoods, and problems with schooling. [Most students in Shanxi Province come from farming families. Eighty to ninety percent of the students at government-funded schools are from poor families. However, the education authorities did not consider the difficulties of the people, and instead of exempting or reducing the existing tuition fees of various schools, they converted government-funded schools such as No. 1 Normal School and No. 1 Women's Normal School into normal junior high schools, collecting additional tuition fees and increasing the burden on students, which led to the fierce student movement. However, there are also other deep-seated reasons and backgrounds, which are described as follows.]

(The Source of the Student Movement) Before 1921, Shanxi education ostensibly adhered to a strict policy. Since the expulsion of the principal at the Provincial No. 1 Middle School in 1922, the authorities have been unable to restrain the laissez-faire tendencies, and it has continued ever since. During the years of party transitions in 1925 and 1926, politicians often used student unity and blind action as tools for seizing power. Since then, student movements have surged, and incidents such as expelling principals, strikes, petitions, demonstrations, and vandalizing the residences of important figures have become commonplace. Principals can only adopt a lenient policy in school affairs and can only adopt a laissez-faire attitude toward students. However, even this does not prevent them from being expelled by students due to other relationships. Although this student movement is still mixed with other reasons, it is mostly a historical development, and its outbreak is not accidental.

(Factions at Shanxi University) Professors at Shanxi University have always been divided into two factions: one is the Western-returned student faction [such as Wang Youchen, president of Shanxi University], Wang Jianxian [dean of the engineering department], etc., and the other is the Eastern-returned student faction, such as Ji Gongquan [dean of the law department and current director of the Education Department], Zhang Guansan, etc. Although these two factions ostensibly claim to cooperate, in reality, they have long been at odds. Regarding the recent incident of students demanding living expenses from the principal, there is a suspicious point: (1) The most that students can demand from the school authorities within the possible range is exemption from tuition fees. How can living expenses be proposed? Even if a subsidy is requested, there are other procedures [requesting subsidies from their respective counties of origin, or directly submitting a petition to the Education Department and the provincial government]. Why make things difficult for the principal? (2) The principal should understand the students' difficulties and forward the students' requests to the Education Department and the provincial government for review. Why was he unable to cope and resign and return home? Based on the above two points, we are convinced that most students were motivated to launch a student movement due to livelihood problems, but some of them are inevitably playing another role, using the masses to make things difficult for the Education Bureau.

(The Normal School Background of No. 1 Middle School) After Wei Riqing, the principal of No. 1 Middle School, was expelled in 1922, his successors often had strong backers. Therefore, when the political situation changed, the principal of No. 1 Middle School was often expelled or resigned voluntarily. Since Cui served as principal, it can be said that there were no other relationships. Cui was a graduate of the Higher Normal School (now the Normal University). He served as an English teacher at No. 1 Middle School and later as the dean of academic affairs for seventeen or eighteen years. Last year, when the Shanxi September 18th Incident [September 18th Incident, the provincial party headquarters shot students petitioning] occurred, the former principal, Liang Tai, fled [Liang Tai was a member of the party executive committee and was involved in the incident]. Cui then succeeded as principal of the school. Since taking office, he has actively reorganized school affairs and has not been lenient with the students. However, when it comes to hiring faculty and staff, he has used graduates from the Higher Normal School to supplement all but a few long-serving and senior people, inevitably leading to a situation where one faction is in control. Although the students' declaration to expel the principal this time accuses Cui of using private connections, it is only a pretext, but it seems that there are also grounds for this.

(No. 1 Normal School and Other Government-Funded Schools) Although the reasons for the expulsion of the principal of No. 1 Normal School are complicated, the cancellation of subsidies and the increase in tuition fees are indeed the main reasons. Normal schools have always been government-funded, and most of the students are from poor families, accounting for seventy to eighty percent. The decline of Shanxi currency and the bankruptcy of the rural economy, coupled with the unusually severe floods this year, have made life difficult in general, especially affecting students' schooling. However, in the autumn of this year, the Education Department suddenly ordered all normal schools to be renamed normal junior high schools, cancelling subsidies and collecting admission fees. New students had to pay a total of more than 45 yuan for all tuition fees, and they had to pay for their own books and board, which led to many poor students dropping out of school. Those who have already enrolled are also struggling to make ends meet. This is the main reason for the normal school student movement. (Taiyuan, November 28)
