All Sectors Concerned About the Safety of Su Bingwen and Others

The Support Association and Others Cabled the National Government for Rescue Yesterday

General Su Bingwen led his troops to resist Japan. Recently, due to pressure from the enemy's superior weapons, he painfully led his troops to retreat into Russian territory. His safety is of great concern to people across the country. The Northeast Anti-Japanese Volunteer Army Support Association cabled the Central Government the night before last, requesting that measures be taken to rescue them. The Liaoning, Jilin, and Heilongjiang People's Committee cabled Su and others yesterday morning to inquire about their whereabouts after leaving the country, but as of 5 pm last night, there was still no reply. The Northeast Anti-Japanese Army Joint Communications Office and the Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, and Rehe Volunteer Army Support Association and other agencies are studying rescue measures, but they feel that it is difficult due to the lack of restoration of diplomatic relations between China and Russia. Most people believe that relief should be carried out by private individuals. The details of the cables are recorded as follows:

The Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, and Rehe Four Provinces Volunteer Army Support Association held a meeting last night and sent a cable to the National Government, which read: "To the Honorable Executive Yuan of the Nanjing National Government: The Northeast has been occupied for more than a year, and Rehe is in imminent danger. The people of various places are unwilling to be subjugated and have formed volunteer armies. However, the government has not provided any assistance in terms of guns, ammunition, or funds. The volunteer armies have been fighting hard for years. Recently, the Japanese invaders have used the forces of the whole country to besiege our isolated and helpless volunteer armies. General Su Bingwen's troops retreated into Russian territory due to running out of ammunition and supplies. The people of the whole country share a deep grief. The survival of the nation is at stake. We earnestly request that you make a quick plan to provide prompt assistance, especially to General Su's troops. We await your orders with grief and impatience. Respectfully, Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, and Rehe Volunteer Army Support Association, Yang."

The National Joint Association of Patriotic Organizations from All Walks of Life cabled the Soviet government in Moscow yesterday, saying: (The previous part omitted) "General Su Bingwen, commander-in-chief of our country's patriotic army, who is fighting for the survival of the nation and for the righteousness of mankind, led more than 4,000 soldiers and patriotic people to retreat into your country's territory due to the violent oppression of Japanese imperialism. Your country is a revolutionary country and its purpose is to help weak nations. Please provide prompt rescue and assistance, and please find a way to escort them to Shanghai from Vladivostok, so that they can serve in the future. Then, our 400 million people will be extremely grateful. Respectfully, the National Joint Association of Patriotic Organizations from All Walks of Life, Yin, Yu."

The United Association of Patriotic Organizations sent an urgent cable to Su Bingwen and others yesterday, which read: "To General Su Bingwen and all officers and soldiers, and displaced people: The Japanese invaders are brutal, cutting off land and slaughtering people. Fortunately, the volunteer armies have sworn to fight to the death. Their prestige has spread far and wide, shocking the world. Recently, due to months of hard fighting and running out of ammunition and supplies, it has become difficult to resist. They fought bloody battles and retreated painfully. Their loyalty will be remembered forever. Their courageous spirit of eliminating the enemy and their sacrifice will be successful. All of our people admire them. The Chinese people in the current situation in China can only find victory and survival through continuous struggle and continued desperate efforts. At present, the only principle for saving the country is to resist whether we win or lose, and to fight desperately whether we live or die. We believe that the failure of you all this time is the inevitable result of the current resistance, and it is by no means an unexpected event, so there is no need to worry. We can only increase our efforts because of failure, and double our fire because the enemy is strong. We are determined to live and die, and never stop. Let us see how long the violence of the enemy can last. You have been reduced to foreign lands for the sake of the country and the nation. The surviving people cannot sleep or eat, and they are indignant and want to die. In addition to urgently finding ways to provide relief, we sincerely send this cable to express our condolences. We respectfully hope that you will take care of yourselves for the sake of the country and wait for the next time. Shanghai United Association of Patriotic Organizations, Standing Directors Shen Zuru, Chen Yafu, Zhang Tianbai, Chen Peide, Zhang Yichen, Wang Hanliang, etc., bowed."

The Northeast Volunteer Army Transportation Team issued a circular yesterday, which read: "To all public organizations and compatriots from all walks of life in the country: The Northeast has been occupied for more than a year. Fortunately, our anti-Japanese generals have been unyielding and brave in their resistance. Although the enemy is stubborn, their goals have not been achieved. Now, the bad news has come that we have learned that General Su Bingwen's troops, the isolated army resisting Japan in Heilongjiang, have been forced to retreat due to running out of ammunition and supplies, and they will be transferred to Russian territory to seek a way back to China. Upon hearing this, we were filled with grief. We hope that all compatriots in the country will refer to the cable from the troops and act on the principle that everyone is responsible for the rise and fall of the country, quickly provide assistance so that the brave anti-Japanese warriors can continue their former ambitions. Our team is about to depart, and all team members are willing to go to the righteous cause and dedicate themselves to the country. They can help with the transportation projects of the volunteer army. As long as there is a breath left, we vow not to return alive. We hope that people from all walks of life will provide guidance from time to time, so that we can follow it. We are anxiously waiting."

The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce cabled the government yesterday, requesting that it quickly find ways to rescue the generals and soldiers. The original cable read: "To the Honorable Executive Yuan, Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and Ministry of Transportation of the Nanjing National Government: Recently, we received a cable from Su Bingwen, Zhang Dianjiu, Xie Ke, Jin Kuibi, Wang Erzhan, Wu Delin, Sun Lin, Dong Shuhong, Gu Junling, Lang Guochen, Yin Shengzuan, and others from Hailar, which briefly stated (the original text is omitted). Based on this, we should cable your honorable Yuan, Ministry, and Department for review. We earnestly request that you quickly find ways to rescue them. Respectfully, Chairman of the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce, Lin Kanghou, bowed."

Mayor Wu's Speech on Great Shanghai

Mainly Unplanned and Deformed Development

Future Reliance on Citizen Cooperation for Rapid Advancement

The evening before last, at 7 o'clock, Mayor Wu Tiecheng delivered a speech on the present and future of Great Shanghai at the Western YMCA on Jing'an Temple Road. It was translated by Municipal Secretary Zhang Dingrong. Details of his speech are recorded below: Today, I have this opportunity to talk about the current situation of our city in a short time. The topic is "The Present and Future of Great Shanghai." I hope you will provide guidance.

(The Present and Future of Great Shanghai) In our ideal, the future Great Shanghai, even if it cannot become a utopian city, is driven by the trend of the times. The great achievements of urban construction in various countries around the world will not only be the largest port in the East but also comparable to the most prosperous cities in the world. All industries, commerce, and international trade will reach unlimited development, and guests will come and enjoy themselves, forgetting to return. I know that the mayor at that time must be an outstanding talent to be competent, and judging from the complexity of his duties and the amount of social interaction, it is certain that he cannot be as leisurely as I am tonight. Although the above is an ideal, it is not difficult to realize. Looking at the current situation and history, the rapid progress of municipal administration in our city in the past is not inferior to that of any city in the world. However, this is not entirely the result of the efforts of the citizens of the city, but a deformed development without a plan. Therefore, if all future facilities can be implemented according to plan, and Chinese and foreign citizens cooperate sincerely, the speed of progress and the beauty of the results can be imagined. It is not surprising that the citizens and the government have not made much effort in the past. In Chinese history, there is no new urban organization, and people living in cities do not participate in administration. In other words, people are passive or negative about politics.

(Chinese Municipal Administration Started in Guangzhou) Chinese municipal administration started in Guangzhou. On February 15th of the tenth year of the Republic of China, the Guangdong Provincial Government announced the "Provisional Regulations of Guangzhou Municipality," designating the entire Guangzhou Municipality as a municipal administrative district, directly under the provincial government. Under the mayor, there were six bureaus: finance, public security, health, public works, and education, responsible for various matters of urban facilities. A municipal council was established to give citizens the opportunity to participate in municipal administration. Since then, all parts of the country have risen up and paid attention. Since its establishment, the city has made rapid progress, with wide roads, grand buildings, and other facilities, which are excellent. Those who have visited Guangzhou can all attest to this.

(Past Shortcomings and Current Facilities) Shanghai followed Guangzhou and was designated as a special municipality directly under the Executive Yuan by the National Government in July of the sixteenth year of the Republic of China. The foundation of our city was established. Before the sixteenth year, although Shanghai had the organization of the Commercial Port Supervisory Office, its scope was narrow and its time was temporary, with little development to speak of. Our city was established not long ago, and its age is young, like a toddler who can only walk and cannot run fast. Thanks to the efforts of successive mayors and the assistance of citizens, it has taken shape and is worthy of being a lively and clever child. The future development is limitless. If we want to know the future Great Shanghai, it seems that we must first briefly describe the past performance of this infant and the shortcomings in its environment, so as to examine and verify. According to the statistics, the total area of Shanghai is 494.69 square kilometers. If the two special districts are added, it totals 527.51 square kilometers. However, in such a vast area, things have never been unified. Taking the area under the jurisdiction of the municipal government as an example, before the sixteenth year of the Republic of China, there were separate districts of Nanshi, Zhabei, and the rural area, each doing its own thing. It was not until the establishment of the municipal government that unification was achieved, and administrative and construction efficiency began to improve. In this short period of five years, I would like to use statistics to briefly cite several auspicious signs as proof of the facts. The roads in Shanghai before the sixteenth year of the Republic of China were 153.95 kilometers long, with an area of 1,504,293 square meters. Now, they are 303.93 kilometers long, with an area of 3,179,486 square meters. In five years, the length has increased by 149.98 kilometers, and the area has increased by 1,675,193 square meters. The ditches have also increased by 31.29 kilometers in five years. In terms of electricity supply, the city had 12,911 kilowatts before the sixteenth year of the Republic of China. Now, it has 26,805 kilowatts, an increase of 13,894 kilowatts in five years. There were originally 3,758 street lights, and now there are 8,301, an increase of 4,543. In terms of water supply, the two companies in Nanshi and Zhabei supplied a total of 65,200 cubic meters in the sixteenth year of the Republic of China. Now, they supply a total of 93,385 cubic meters, an increase of 28,185 cubic meters in five years. As for the improvement of water quality, it is particularly significant. In the sixteenth year of the Republic of China, Zhabei tap water had 8,208 bacteria per cubic millimeter. Now, it has been reduced to 36. Nanshi tap water had 3,498 bacteria per cubic millimeter in the sixteenth year of the Republic of China. Now, it has been reduced to 50. In terms of transportation facilities, the most significant progress since the sixteenth year of the Republic of China is the municipal ferry. Five or six years ago, if we wanted to go from Puxi to Pudong, we had no other choice but to use small ferries or sampans. The inconvenience of ordinary travel had reached its extreme, and the danger was increasing daily. Furthermore, Pudong is an important area of the city, but its development has been difficult due to the lack of close connection with Puxi. We have always proposed building a bridge, but due to the huge cost, it is still a pie in the sky. In order to seek rescue from the above, the municipal government decided to establish a ferry service. The distance across the river is suitable, with a total of seven ships. The fares are low, the management is strict, and the sailing is punctual and fast, which is extremely convenient for passengers. Its achievements have exceeded our expectations. Last year alone, there were more than 4.4 million passengers. Now, we are actively preparing to expand the cross-river ferry to meet the needs. The advantages of the municipal ferry are not only a supplement to transportation but also two other important points: ① The population of Shanghai is large, and daily vegetables and other agricultural products rely entirely on the supply from the surrounding rural areas. The more sources of supply, the lower the prices, and the cost of living in the city will not rise. Therefore, the ability of the municipal ferry to easily transport agricultural products from Pudong to Puxi has a great impact on the lives of citizens. ② Every summer, citizens suffer from the lack of places to rest and enjoy the coolness. Since the opening of the ferry, thousands of Chinese and foreign citizens in Puxi have visited Donghan and Gaoqiao every day. In the future, after the Gaoqiao seaside beach is renovated and improved, that place will become the only summer resort, and its benefits to the citizens will certainly be immeasurable. In terms of hygiene and education, the importance of public health in Shanghai is self-evident. The municipal government pays close attention to the health of citizens and the prevention of epidemics. Currently, all meat in the city must be officially inspected by veterinarians before and after slaughter, which was initiated by our municipal government. The widespread implementation of various vaccinations was also first advocated by our municipal government. The serum used is self-made and supplied to the public concessions and the French concession. In the past two or three years, the effectiveness of epidemic prevention has become increasingly apparent. This year, due to the Japanese invasion of Shanghai, the epidemic was contained by making every effort to prevent it, and the city was able to remain safe, which is evident to everyone. Regarding education, since educational administration has always been inconsistent, the municipal government has been engaged in reorganizing and unifying the organization, enriching equipment, and improving the treatment of teachers since its establishment. There are currently 180 municipal primary schools and 5 middle schools, among which many primary and secondary school students have been newly established in the past five years. Previously, the city's education expenditure was only several hundred thousand yuan per year. In the past five years, it has increased to 1.2 million yuan, accounting for more than 10% of the city's revenue. It is hoped that it will increase to 25% in the future. Although the number of municipal schools and the amount of funding are far from sufficient to meet the needs of the entire city, they are several times higher than those of other cities and remote provinces in the country, which also shows the magnitude of the city's scope. The financial problem is the key to all facilities. Although the financial situation of our city is not sufficient now, it is not the phenomenon that should exist. The annual income and expenditure of our city are offset, not only without loss but also with surplus. This is all due to the financial reorganization in previous years. Five years ago, the income was only two or three million yuan, but it has recently increased to more than seven million yuan. If the January 28 Incident had not occurred, the city's income could have exceeded last year's budget by the end of June, reaching 10 million yuan, which can be proved by various facts. Unexpectedly, the sound of gunfire turned everything into a bubble, which is very frustrating. However, I believe that the original state will soon be restored, so that the future Great Shanghai can be realized as soon as possible. There are still many other municipal facilities and problems that will be explained in detail when the heads of various bureaus come to give speeches in the future, so I will not discuss them for the time being. However, the above points are enough to prove that we have hope for this child.

(Future Improvement Plan) However, in my opinion, the future Great Shanghai has many shortcomings in its current form, and we must seek ways to fundamentally improve it. Now, I would like to put forward one or two points for your discussion: ① Looking at the existing facilities in Shanghai as a whole, there was no overall design at the beginning. I think no one expected the city to reach today's prosperity. Therefore, the streets in various places lack planned regulations. Even if we want to improve it now, it is difficult. In the future, the impact on transportation will inevitably become more apparent. ② In terms of population and commerce, Shanghai has become the third largest city in the world. The number of ships coming to our city this year has reached hundreds of thousands of tons. However, regardless of the size of the ships, they must travel for more than an hour after entering the Huangpu River before they can berth. Sometimes, passengers cannot even land directly. This kind of economic loss and inconvenience is rare in countries around the world. How can we ignore it? The current situation is already like this. If we think about it, what will the congestion and inconvenience be like in 20, 30, or 100 years? Therefore, in this childhood period, for the sake of the adult Great Shanghai, we should use the farthest vision and the greatest determination to jointly build the future Great Shanghai and improve the current environment. The Shanghai Municipal Government, in view of this, decided on a unified plan for the future Great Shanghai a year ago, starting with the construction of the city center, and at the same time planning the commercial port and the Huangpu port entrance bridge. Experts from European and American city design companies were invited to contribute their opinions, and they all agreed. Now, we are actively carrying out the plan. In the future, the benefits of realizing this strategy for the citizens of Shanghai and international trade will certainly be immeasurable. Some say, "The environment in Shanghai is already very good, and the Shanghai child is also very healthy. Why not let it develop naturally, but use this kind of plan to restrain it?" I dare to answer, "If this child does not have disciplined and orderly training, the body and brain will inevitably develop abnormally, and even if the palm passes, people will be sufficient to swell the abdomen, or even suffer from hundreds of diseases that cannot be cured. As nannies, since we have seen this, how can we be willing to sacrifice the future fate of this child?" According to the current plan, the administrative area, commercial area, industrial area, and residential area of the future Great Shanghai will all be clearly defined. In terms of transportation, they will be interconnected, making travel convenient. Residents can be free from the disgust of heavy smoke and poisonous gas, and factories can be free from the restrictions of development. Ships can enter and berth at the docks immediately, and goods can be loaded directly onto trains and transported to various provinces for sale. In addition to the Pudong ferry, there will also be a bridge and railway connection. The benefits of these kinds of benefits are truly endless. However, this plan does not abandon the existing prosperous areas, and the roads in various places can be connected. Therefore, even if the population and commerce increase tenfold or dozens of times, there is no need to worry that they cannot be accommodated. Now, I will briefly describe the plan as follows: ① Water and land transportation. In terms of waterways, the Huangpu River is actually the main stream. The existing docks in the port are already very cramped in location and too far from the port, which takes time to navigate. In the future, with the development of commerce and the increasing number of ships, it will not be enough to build large-scale harbors to meet the needs. Therefore, the location of the future dock area will be in the Wusong area, and the location along the coast of Pudong can be used for the expansion of the commercial port. At present, inland transportation mostly takes the Wusong River. In the future, this river will also be unable to accommodate all ships coming to Shanghai. Therefore, the Wusong Bay and Zhaobang will in fact be the hub of inland transportation in the future, which is also expected. If a canal can be excavated at a suitable location to connect with the Wusong River, transshipment will be even more convenient. As for the land, the existing railway lines are far away from the waterways and docks, making it difficult to connect water and land. Therefore, after the city center is built, the location of the commercial port will be determined at the same time, and the railway lines in Shanghai must be rerouted. It is assumed that Zhenru will be the transportation terminal, and a branch line will be built from here, passing north through the Rucheng Hujiazhuang and east along the southern bank of the Luzaobang to the Wusong area, connecting with the South Port. Furthermore, an elevated railway will be built from Zhenru, passing through Pengpu and reaching Jiangwan, which will be the future Shanghai Central Station. Then, passengers and light goods can be directly transported into the city center area. The prosperity of the North Station can still be maintained, and the Shanghai-Hangzhou railway line will remain the same as before. However, starting from Shanghai Station, the railway line will be extended to Dongjiadu, and the ferry to Pudong will be built directly north to the bridge, so that transportation in Pudong can also be made more convenient. ② Road system. Regarding the roads in the city center area, I will briefly describe them as follows: A. Building main roads connecting the commercial port railway and various districts. These roads are generally very wide, either connecting to the future commercial port or connecting to the future central station, or connecting to the current concession and other urban areas, like starlight radiating in all directions, with the city center area in the center, controlling the overall situation. B. Building ordinary roads to facilitate commerce and residence. The purpose of these roads is to facilitate commerce and transportation in the city center area and its vicinity, and to build them separately to facilitate construction. The planned routes are about 170 kilometers long, and their layout is based on a chessboard style and a spider web style, surrounding the periphery, and determined according to the orthogonality or obliquity of the main roads, so as to ensure that the divided sections are suitable for construction. In addition, due to the climate in this city, it is suitable to face south, so the eastern direction of each section is lengthened to reduce the number of north-south roads. In addition, the sections parallel to the main roads are also lengthened as much as possible to reduce the intersection of ordinary roads and main roads. C. Establishing gardens and sports fields to benefit the health, rest, and recreation of citizens. For the sake of the health and spiritual cultivation of citizens, the existing rivers in the city center area and its vicinity are fully utilized, and plots of land are delineated to set up large gardens and open spaces, and efforts are made to make them suitable for mutual connection to embellish the city and facilitate sightseeing. Zoning plan: According to the current zoning plan for the entire city, the city center area and the area south to the old city of Nanshi are commercial areas, the north is the commercial port area, and the west is the residential area. The city center area, according to the general rules of urban organization, should be the location of administrative organs and important buildings. Now, the zoning plan for the city center area is briefly described as follows: Political District: All administrative organs and important public buildings should be located in the core and superior locations of the city to show solemnity and prosperity. The central part of the city center area is the intersection of two main roads, and there are gardens embellishing it, which is most suitable for being designated as a political area. The municipal government and its affiliated bureaus, the municipal party headquarters, the municipal council, the library, the museum, the art gallery, etc., should all be built here. Commercial District: In the northern part of the city center area, close to the commercial port and connected to the passenger terminal, the prosperity of commerce in the future can be predicted. Therefore, a large part of it is designated as a commercial area to meet the trend of development. In addition, the land along the main roads is heavily trafficked, and building shops here is both profitable and can limit the residential areas behind, so as to avoid noise. Therefore, it is also designated as a commercial area. Residential District: Except for the parts that have been designated as political districts and commercial districts in the city center area and its vicinity, the rest are designated as residential areas. The residential area is divided into A, B, and C. Type A residential area is for building residences for merchants and others, and it seeks quietness. Therefore, its location is near the gardens and open spaces. Moreover, since the supply and demand for this type of residence is relatively small, the area is small. Type B residential area is for building ordinary residences, and the supply and demand are relatively large, so the area is larger. The above plan for the city center area is now being carried out. The construction of the municipal government building started last year and could have been completed in July of this year, but it was obstructed by the January 28 Incident and must be completed in May of next year. At that time, the municipal government and its affiliated bureaus will be prepared to move in to show the realization of the future Great Shanghai. My discussion here is very interesting, and I deeply believe that you also have great hopes for the future Great Shanghai. However, in order to make this plan a reality as soon as possible and ensure that all construction is not hindered, the concerted action of all citizens is indispensable. All those who live in this city, regardless of their nationality, have the obligation to build Great Shanghai, and should regard Shanghai as their homeland. The citizens of Great Shanghai and the glory of Great Shanghai are the glory of all citizens. I am willing to join you in wishing success in the future.

New Commander Minai Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday

Loudly Singing the Old Tune of Sino-Japanese Friendship

(Meeting Representatives) Yesterday morning at 8 o'clock, the new commander of the Japanese Navy's Third Fleet, Vice Admiral Minai, arrived in Shanghai on the flagship Izumo and berthed at River Tube No. 78 in the Huangpu River. Commander Sakano, Rear Admiral Sugimoto, Colonel Shima, Lieutenant Colonel Higuchi, and others arrived at the ship at 10:30 a.m. to welcome him. Minister Arima Yoshi also sent Military Attaché Kitaoka, along with Japanese Consul Ishishe, Administrative Committee Chairman Yasui, and representatives of the Japanese community, to visit the ship. A total of more than 40 government and civilian representatives boarded the ship one after another. At 1:00 p.m., they took photos on the ship and left. Minai said that he had been to Shanghai when the May 30th Incident occurred, and it has been several years since then. His adjutant Ishikawa and paymaster Okada also came with him.

(Reviewing the Fleet) After arriving in Shanghai, Minai immediately issued a notice to review the four newly dispatched ships of the 27th Fleet, including the Hishi and Ashi, in Shanghai starting at 2:00 p.m. today. Tomorrow morning, he will review the Shanghai Special Naval Landing Force. On the 12th, he will review the First Overseas Dispatch Fleet's flagship Atago. In the afternoon, he will review the destroyers of the 24th Fleet, including the Yanagi and Momo. After the 12th, he will go to Nanjing and other ports along the Yangtze River at a later date.

(Visiting the Mayor) At 10:00 a.m. today, Minai, accompanied by an interpreter, first visited the commanders of the British, American, French, and Italian ships in Shanghai. Then, he went to Gaochang Temple to pay a visit to the Chinese Navy authorities. At 2:00 p.m., he went to visit Minister Arima Yoshi and paid a visit to the commanders of the foreign forces stationed in Shanghai. After 3:00 p.m., he went to the Municipal Government to meet Mayor Wu. Our Mayor Wu has scheduled to return the visit at 11:00 a.m. on the 10th.

(Issuing a Declaration) Upon arriving in Shanghai, Minai issued a declaration to the Japanese residents in Shanghai, which roughly stated that on the first of this month, he was appointed as the commander of the new Third Fleet, shouldering the important responsibility of guarding Shanghai and the Yangtze River. He arrived in Shanghai today and recalled that two cycles of sixty years ago, he served as the commander of the First Overseas Dispatch Fleet in Shanghai. Now, he revisits the old place and meets with you again. In this extraordinary time when the Manchurian and Shanghai Incidents have occurred, you have worked hard for the sake of patriotism, and you also hope that Japan and China will cooperate with each other to ensure peace in the East. I will follow the general policy of the previous commander to restore the Sino-Japanese relationship to normal, but I deeply hope that the Japanese people will give their support.

Feng Yuxiang Telegraphed Shanghai to Defend Zhou Lisheng's Remarks

Stating He Only Visited the Forbidden City Once

Times Have Changed and Have Nothing to Do With Feng

Central Committee Member Feng Yuxiang, telegraphed Shanghai from Zhangjiakou, saying, "To the attention of all compatriots through various newspapers: Recently, I have read an article in the December 2nd issue of the Beiping World Daily and the fourth page, containing remarks by Supervisory Committee Member Zhou Lisheng regarding the investigation of the Forbidden City. Among them, it is stated that, 'According to personal opinion, the exchange of antiques is unavoidable. In the Qing Dynasty and the Feng Yuxiang era, when antiques were not registered, similar forgery malpractices were most likely to occur.' I was deeply shocked after reading it. Supervisory Committee Member Zhou Lisheng is also speaking responsibly to the press, so he should not be so vague in his words. During the expulsion of Puyi in the thirteenth year of the Republic of China, although it was carried out by the National Army, the reception of the Forbidden City was handled by social groups and educators such as Mr. Li Shizeng. I only visited the Forbidden City once in the seventeenth year of the Republic of China, when the Northern Expedition was completed. How can there be a so-called 'Feng Yuxiang era'? Moreover, after the Qing Dynasty's Xuantong ruled Beijing, it went through Yuan, Li, Cao, Duan, and others, which had nothing to do with me. Even referring to the period after Puyi left the palace, those who held power in Beijing also had nothing to do with me from beginning to end, so there can be no so-called 'Feng Yuxiang era'. I am afraid that the people of the country will be misled by the words of Committee Member Zhou, so I must quickly defend myself. May the people of the country understand. Feng Yuxiang"

Although it also involves civilian property, there are no villages in that area, and the losses suffered by the people are relatively light. Now, the plan has suddenly been changed to acquire the entire Zhao's Garden village. The area is full of villagers' houses, and they plant flowers and trees for a living. The branches and trunks are rooted in the ground, and they are old and difficult to transplant. Once relocated, it is tantamount to abandoning them. The situation is different from the farmland that can be exchanged. This move is no less than depriving them of their source of food and clothing, and the situation is truly pitiful. We humbly believe that it is an unavoidable move for the country to build public utilities and acquire land, but if a way can be found to bypass it, the aim is to make the people suffer less losses. Now that there is the original acquired land available for use, then we should consider both sides and take the lesser of two evils. According to the letter, the situation is reasonable, and we hereby telegraph your department for review and approval, and to order the railway bureau to follow the original land acquisition plan so that the villagers will suffer less losses. It is for the public benefit. The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce kowtows."

The text reads as follows: "The petition is submitted regarding the Railway Department's unauthorized requisition of civilian land for the construction of a connecting station, with the purpose of seeking profit, and requesting assistance to relieve the plight of the people. The Railway Department is implementing a fifty-year plan for the revitalization of two railway lines in Greater Shanghai, requisitioning civilian land between the Zhenru and Pengpu districts to build a connecting station. This matter concerns national construction, and the people are wholeheartedly supportive and have no grounds for objection. However, the Railway Department's plan does not take into account both national planning and the livelihood of the people, and its implementation would leave thousands of families destitute. However, two months have passed, and the Railway Department has not provided a clear response, nor has it openly announced the plan in accordance with the land acquisition law. Its actions are perverse and deeply alarming. The Council, as the leader of the representatives of the citizens, has a keen understanding of the hardships of the citizens and dares to enumerate the circumstances, hoping for your consideration. It is rumored that the reason for avoiding that area is that internal personnel have purchased a large amount of land there. Although there is no evidence to support this, such measures clearly reveal signs of malpractice. This is the first reason why the people refuse to acknowledge the construction of the connecting station. Internal and external troubles are constant, and the national treasury is empty. The people's livelihood is in decline. The people of the country are well aware of whether such large-scale construction is essential to the national economy and whether the country can afford it. The eagerness to implement the plan reveals the intention to borrow money at a discount under the guise of construction. This is the second reason why the people refuse to acknowledge the construction of the connecting station. The development of Shanghai is currently expanding towards the east and west, not the north and south. If it is said that setting up a station is enough to promote prosperity, it is doubtful whether this is possible when municipal administration has not been revitalized and the situation is not peaceful. Looking at the Shanghai-Hangzhou station in southern Shanghai and the Railway Bureau in northern Shanghai, the carriages are like clouds, and the nearby city should be thriving. However, it remains desolate, which is clear evidence. Even if it is said that the relocation of the station is a plan for fifty years later and cannot be compared to the current situation, the land will be requisitioned, the houses will be destroyed, and the basis of life will be completely destroyed. Such a large sacrifice is being made for non-essential construction. This is the third reason why the people refuse to acknowledge the construction of the connecting station. It would be better to set up the station in Jiangwan and connect it to the city center, which would lead to far greater development than in the interior, and would be more economical for the Railway Department itself. This is the fourth reason why the people refuse to acknowledge the construction of the connecting station. In summary, there are more than 700 households in the villages, with more than 2,000 people, who either cultivate flowers and trees or grow vegetables. They live in peace and harmony. If the plan is rashly implemented, the people will have no land to cultivate and no homes to live in, and the flowers and trees, which have been cultivated diligently for forty or fifty years or planted for six or seven years, and only yield a meager profit, will be turned to nothing. The people are willing to give their lives and offer their blood to plead with the Council to consider the people's difficulties, uphold justice, and fight for the relocation of the Railway Department, which disregards the people's situation and seizes civilian land. The people will not yield and will not give up. In submitting this petition, we cannot express our urgent desire to await your orders. Respectfully submitted to the Speaker of the Municipal Council, Shi. The petitioners are Hou Xuanqing, Zhao Youting, etc."

Robbery of a Cigarette and Paper Shop, Two Female Customers Shot Dead

Shouting "Catch the Robber" Resulted in a Tragic Death on the Spot

丨The Robbers Were Murderous...Not Uttering a Word丨

A robbery occurred in Xian Gua Street outside the South City the night before. The victim was the Yongtai Chang cigarette and paper shop. A total of more than 100 yuan was robbed. The robbers shot and killed a female customer before leaving. The details are recorded below:

Three Robbers Break into Cigarette and Paper Shop Zhang Yaoting, a native of Zhenjiang, runs the Yongtai Chang cigarette and paper shop at No. 42, opposite Xingren Lane, Xian Gua Street outside Xiaodongmen. At around 8:00 PM the night before, three robbers suddenly arrived. One robber was wearing a blue cloth short shirt and pants, and the other two robbers were wearing black short shirts and pants. All were around 30 years old. One of the robbers in the blue cloth short shirt and pants jumped over the counter into the shop, took out a pistol, and warned not to make a sound. The other two robbers stood outside the door as lookouts.

A Woman Holds Silver to Exchange One of the robbers in the shop grabbed more than 50 yuan in banknotes and more than 600 jiao in small silver coins from the drawer of the account table. At that time, Zhang and the people in the shop were all stunned and let the robbers search. Peng Zuo, a 21-year-old woman from Huai'an, lived in the Yangshupu area of ​​eastern Shanghai. She had recently come to her mother's house in Laotaiping Lane in the South City to linger for a few days. After dinner the night before, she planned to go to Xiaodongmen to buy goods. When walking through Xingren Lane, she suddenly realized that she was lacking in small change, so she held a silver dollar to Yongtai Chang for exchange.

Peng Zuo Dies from Gunshot Wound At the same time, the robber in the blue cloth short shirt and pants happened to get the banknotes and jumped out of the counter with the loot. He suddenly saw the woman standing by the counter and planned to rob the silver dollar in her hand. The woman was shocked and shouted "Catch the robber!" Unexpectedly, as soon as she finished speaking, the robber pulled the trigger. There was a loud bang, and the woman fell to the ground from the gunshot. The bullet entered from the front chest and came out from the back. Blood was flowing profusely, and she fainted from the pain. The robbers fled in all directions after seeing the bloody case.

Police Officers Patrol but Find Nothing Zhang Tingju, the police officer in the 25th guard post near the area, was standing at his post when he suddenly heard gunshots. He immediately came to the source of the sound. At this time, the district chief of the district also rushed to the scene with district staff after hearing the report, and patrolled everywhere, but the robbers had gone far away, so they found nothing. The police sent the injured to Shanghai Hospital for treatment. However, the injury was fatal, and she died before she could be treated. Yesterday, the local police reported to the Shanghai District Court for an autopsy.

The Bandits Learned the Silent Ways of the Jin People When the robbers were robbing, they never spoke a word, but glared with murderous intent and searched and robbed in one fell swoop. It can also be said to be a unique aspect of the robbery case.

After Zhang Shiming's Death, the Disturbance周妙英Obtains the Final Victory

Qu'an and Miaoying are Definitely Mother and Son, the Supreme Court Reverses the Judgments of the Previous Two Trials

The late Zhang Shiming, a wealthy man from Nanxun, married Zhou Miaoying, a woman from Suzhou, as his concubine, and had a son named Qu'an, who ranked ninth. After Kouming's death, Miaoying and the main wife, Xu, disagreed, so she rented a house to live in, while Qu'an was raised by Xu. The Xu family married their niece to him two years ago. Because they were afraid that Miaoying would come out to obstruct the marriage, they also kept the marriage secret. Afterwards, Miaoying found out and filed a lawsuit against Qu'an and Zhang Xu, asking to confirm the relationship between mother and son. During the first trial, the defendants presented evidence that Zhou Miaoying had taken 40,000 yuan as a fee to sever the relationship. As a result, Zhou Miaoying lost the lawsuit. Zhou refused to accept it and appealed to the Second Branch of the High Court, but suffered another defeat. Zhou then hired lawyer Yuan Yang'an to file an appeal with the Supreme Court. The Supreme Court has investigated and ruled that the judgments of the previous two trials shall be reversed, and that Zhou Miaoying and Zhang Qu'an are indeed related as mother and son. The judgment is recorded below:

(Main text) The original judgment and the first trial judgment are both reversed. It is confirmed that the appellant Zhang Qu'an still has a mother-son relationship. The litigation costs of all levels of trial shall be borne by the defendant and appellant. (Reason) The appellant Zhang Qu'an in this case was originally the son of the appellant when she was Zhang Shiming's concubine. The appellant now claims that after she gave birth to Qu'an, Zhang Shiming remarried Zhang Xu as

her successor. She was abused and not allowed to live together. She forced Shiming to die in the 16th year of the Republic of China. Xu actually包園包園Qu'an, not allowing him to communicate with the appellant. Later, she订婚订婚 Qu'an without letting the appellant know about it. She requested that the relationship between the appellant and Qu'an be confirmed as mother and son. According to the regulations of Article 287 of the Civil Procedure Regulations cited by the previous court in Jiangsu Province, a lawsuit to confirm the establishment or non-establishment of a legal relationship cannot be filed unless the plaintiff has a legal interest in the confirmation judgment (Article 238, Paragraph 1 of the Civil Procedure Law has the same provisions). This type of confirmation lawsuit is originally based on the fact that the existence of the legal relationship is unclear. In this case, the fact that the appellant Zhang Qu'an is the biological son of the appellant is not denied by him. According to the law, even if the mother breaks away from the relationship with the father, the son she bears has no duty to sever the relationship with the mother. Therefore, the relationship between mother and son is still existing according to the law. However, the appellant argued in the first trial and repeatedly claimed that the appellant had long severed the relationship with the family of Shi Ming and had voluntarily signed an agreement in the 17th year of the Republic of China, giving her 40,000 yuan as a severance fee for everything related to the biological mother who had left the family, so there was no longer any relationship to speak of, etc. By the time of the original trial, when the appellant's agent asked whether she admitted that she was the biological mother, Zhang Qu'an did not answer. This can be proved by the record. Therefore, whether the mother-son relationship between the appellant Zhang Qu'an and the appellant should continue to exist is clearly still in dispute and is not clear. It cannot be said that the appellant has no need to file a confirmation lawsuit. However, the court only determined that the mother-son relationship had been established because the appellant did not fundamentally deny that the appellant was the mother. The lawsuit was dismissed. The appeal in the second trial still upheld the judgment of the first trial dismissing the lawsuit. The legal views are difficult to consider in agreement. Also, the appellant listed the appellant Zhang Xu as a defendant in the lawsuit, saying that Zhang Qu'an's failure to recognize the appellant as his mother was caused by her deception. Whether the claim is true or not is aside, but it cannot be said that the lawsuit is illegal. The original judgment also misunderstood this point. The appellant requested to reverse the judgments of the first and second trials and make another judgment. It cannot be said that there is no reason. Based on the above discussion and conclusion, the appeal in this case is justified. The judgment is made in accordance with Article 444, Paragraph 1 and Article 446, Section 1 of the Civil Procedure Law, as stated in the main text. Presiding Judge of the Second Civil Tribunal of the Supreme Court, Lin Dingcao, judges耿·Jiang Fukun·Tang Benyin·Lin Zusheng. Clerk Yang Shuyun.

At that time, I was at the entrance of the store, and the scene of the accident was about three storefronts away from me. I saw the car driving very fast, and the deceased was walking from south to north when he was hit by the car. Mr. Zhan then ruled that the body of the unknown man had been hit by car number 5742 and died from a head injury. No family was found, and the body was handed over to the Pushan Villa for burial. The driver, Hideo, is suspected of negligence and should be investigated and dealt with by the police.

The Case of Human-Dog Intercourse

Chen Xinzhai Appeals Against the Original Sentence

Final Hearing Held Yesterday, Sentencing Scheduled

Chen Xinzhai, residing at No. 12, Hongfu Lane, Xinzha Road, works at the Tianyun Tower of the Wing On Company as a diablo performer. His concubine, Chen Lu, has four adopted daughters: Chen Shuanglin, 11 years old; Gui Lin, 8 years old; and Gen Ling and Caiyun, both 6 years old. They are usually taught to sing opera and perform at the New World Company. In July of this year, Detective Sergeant Tang Jian of the Xinzha Police Station discovered that the Chens were taking the four adopted daughters and a small black dog to various hotels within the settlement to perform human-dog sexual acts for profit, an act that harmed public morals. He went to the Chen residence and took the Chens, suspect Liu Xin'san, the four girls, and the small black dog, along with drug paraphernalia, to the police station. Investigations revealed that the Chens had repeatedly taken the humans and the dog to perform at major hotels such as the Oriental, Da Zhonghua, and Shenzhou, with each spectator paying five yuan. The four children were sent to the hospital, where it was confirmed that their hymens were broken. They were then sent to the First Special District Court, where they confessed clearly after repeated interrogations. Judge Wu Tingqi sentenced Chen Xinzhai and Chen Lu to ten years of imprisonment each, acquitted Liu Xin'san, confiscated the drug paraphernalia and dog, and sent the four children to the Jiliang Institute for care. This has been reported in our newspaper before. However, the Chens were dissatisfied with the verdict and hired lawyer Gan Lin to appeal to the Second Branch of the High Court. Their appeal focused solely on the charge of offending public morals, while they expressed agreement with the confiscation of the drug paraphernalia. Yesterday afternoon, Criminal Court President Yu Hua of the Second Branch of the High Court, along with Judges Luo and Guo, presided over the hearing. Lawyer Wang Yaotang represented the police station. President Yu stated that this case concerned public morals, so he ordered that no spectators be allowed. He then asked Chen Xinzhai for the reasons for his dissatisfaction with the first instance verdict. Chen denied any obscene behavior, claiming that the doctors found only abrasions in the girls' lower bodies, but no broken hymens. He argued that the girls were taught opera and practiced techniques, and their lower bodies could easily be scratched inadvertently. He stated that there was no improper behavior. The testimonies of Chen Lu, witness Liu Xin'san, and the child Chen Shuanglin were largely the same as their testimonies in the first instance, so they were omitted. Finally, after arguments between police lawyer Wang Yaotang and appellant's lawyer Gan Lin, President Yu adjourned the hearing and scheduled the sentencing for next Wednesday afternoon.

A Record of the National Government's Flood Relief Committee's Inspection of the Completed Dike Project (10)

(Zhang Gong Dike in Hankou) Jiang Xinshu arrived in Hankou at 6:00 AM on December 3rd. Representatives from the Hubei Provincial Government and public organizations, as well as Public Security Bureau Chief Chen Xizeng, greeted him at the dock. A welcoming arch was erected along the riverbank. The Public Security Bureau and the Provincial Government military band, along with armed police and soldiers, provided music and guarded the dock. More than twenty cars were prepared for the members to ride in. At 9:00 AM, the entire group disembarked and rode in cars along the riverbank to inspect the Hankou riverfront flood control dike. It is a concrete and rebar structure, about seven English miles long, extending from the Customs Wharf to Shenjiaji. It is about four meters wide. The river-facing side is built with stones, and the top is made of water-resistant mortar with iron railings. It is both extremely sturdy and aesthetically pleasing. The dike surface is paved with yellow sand, forming a perfect road. According to Engineering Bureau Chief Yang Silian, the stone used for this section of the project was all transported from Henan, resulting in high costs. The total cost was over 300,000 yuan. It serves as Hankou's front barrier. From Shenjiaji onward, it becomes Zhang Gong Dike, protecting the back of Hankou, extending twelve and a half kilometers. The two dikes connect to form a large circle, with the entire city of Hankou residing safely within. If the dikes are well maintained and protected, Hankou can expect to be free from floods forever. The members walked and rode along the way, praising the beauty of the dike. The cars traveled along the dike, and after passing Shenjiaji, they entered Zhang Gong Dike. The surface of Zhang Gong Dike is even wider than the flood control dike, about seven meters wide. The side facing the water is also a stone slope. The cleanliness of the road proves the diligence of the authorities in maintaining the dike. Halfway along Zhang Gong Dike, they got off the cars at Gusushu, a small town with densely packed thatched huts. A simple welcoming arch was erected, and every household hung the national flag in welcome. The Provincial Government and public organizations set up tents and long tables on the dike to serve tea to the members. Hubei Provincial Government Chairman Xia Douyin and representatives from the Hubei Flood Relief Committee also personally attended to welcome them. Shortly after, they boarded the cars again and traveled along the dike, winding into the city, stopping in front of the Hankou Orphanage. Commissioner Li led them inside for a tour. It was already 10:30 AM.

(Visiting the Orphanage) The Hankou Orphanage is located in the original Charity Association building. The buildings are quite large, and there are currently 340 orphans, about 90 of whom are girls. The oldest is 17 years old, and the youngest is 6 years old. It was officially established on October 1st of this year. Chen Jiyu, the Deputy Director of the Hubei Flood Relief Committee, serves as the Director of the orphanage. There are over 20 faculty and staff members. The daily operating expenses are about 3,000 yuan, subsidized by the Flood Relief Committee and other charitable organizations. Director Chen led them on a tour of the various facilities, including the orphanage workshops, where the orphans are taught various small crafts such as wicker weaving, rope making, and embroidery. The girls wear blue cotton-padded uniforms and blue cloth hats, and they are very lively. There is a children's farm for practical cultivation, and a children's city government for orphans to practice self-governance. They also visited the dormitories, classrooms, and dining hall. All the arrangements were well-organized and clean, suitable for children to live in. The walls were covered with pictures depicting common etiquette and knowledge, such as "Do not make noise while eating," "Wash your hands before eating," and "Walk slowly on the stairs and do not speak loudly." There is also a Boy Scout organization, wearing yellow cloth military uniforms. They have a headquarters and a lookout tower, and the sentries are only seven or eight years old, but they know how to salute. Xia Douyin praised them after the tour. At 12:00 PM, there was a gathering in the auditorium. Chu Minyi, Xia Douyin, and Sun Faxu all gave sincere speeches, encouraging the orphans. Finally, Commissioner Li gave a detailed report on the establishment of the orphanage. At 1:00 PM, they returned to the Yangtze River Hotel for lunch. At 2:00 PM, the entire group crossed the river to Wuchang to inspect the Wu-Jing Dike. At 8:00 PM, they were invited by the Hubei Provincial Government and the Hubei Flood Relief Committee to a banquet at the Golden City Bank Building.

(Li Zushen Initiates) The orphans in the orphanage are all orphans of families affected by last year's floods. The original initiator was Commissioner Li Zushen of the National Flood Relief Committee. In September of last year, he started the Shanghai Zhabei Flood Orphans Shelter and invited the China Child Welfare Association to handle the childcare work. The Association set up four departments: education, nutrition, health, and recreation. General Secretary Wu Weide personally went to Wuhu, Jiujiang, and Hankou in November of last year to investigate the situation of the affected children. At that time, nearly 260,000 disaster victims were sheltered near Wuhan, and the number of affected children accounted for about one-third. About 4,000 children were completely without parents. At that time, the weather was suddenly cold, and the Flood Relief Committee's finances were very tight. They had no choice but to cancel the provision of four liters of rice per disaster victim, half for the disaster children, as resettlement funds. Since the disaster victims had nowhere to go, incidents of selling disaster children occurred. Wu heard about this and consulted Commissioner Li Zushen, proposing to donate funds to establish an orphanage to shelter the disaster children. Li strongly urged its success and took out 4,000 yuan from his own pocket as start-up funds. With the support of General Zhu Ziqiao, the Wuhan Disaster Orphans Education and Care Center of the China Child Welfare Association was established in Wuchang in late December. Li Zushen was appointed as the honorary director, and Wu Weide served as the director. The China Child Welfare Association, the National Flood Relief Committee, the Hubei Flood Relief Committee, the Shanghai YMCA, the National Association, the Wuchang YMCA, Wuhan University, the Shanghai National Medical College, and Huazhong University in Wuchang were invited as initiators to cooperate in the operation. Initially, 300 orphans were sheltered. About 200 orphans were later claimed by their families, and the project was completely closed by the end of the year. All the property and 135 disaster children were transferred to the current orphanage, expanding its scale to what it is today. It is heard that a board of directors is currently being organized to raise funds, hoping to make it permanent. When the League of Nations Investigation Team visited Hankou, they visited the orphanage founded by Li, and Lord Lytton expressed his appreciation, saying to Commissioner Li Zushen, "You are truly someone who can make a great contribution to the country." When Commissioner Li accompanied the entire group on the tour this time, the Tai orphans were all familiar with him. When they saw Li, they shouted "Mr. Li" and rushed forward, as if they were family members. Li is a truly enthusiastic person, and his contribution to benefiting society is undeniable.

(A Glimpse of the Wu-Jing Dike) The Hankou flood control dike was built by the Hubei Flood Relief Committee, and Zhang Gong Dike originally belonged to the Fifth District project but was handled by the Hubei Flood Relief Committee. At 2:00 PM, the entire group crossed the river to Wuchang. After landing at Baishazhou and walking several hundred paces, they reached the Wu-Jing Dike. The dike is an earthen dike, ten meters wide, allowing two cars to drive side by side. It is twenty kilometers long, stretching from Jingkou in the west to Wuchang in the east. The project is extremely sturdy and is one of the main dike projects in Hubei. They returned to Hankou at 5:00 PM. (Money Hua reported from Hankou on the evening of December 3rd)

From the 14th of this month to the 6th of next month

The Shanghai General Station of the Domestic Radio Station in this city, in accordance with previous years, will hold New Year's telegrams as the New Year's Day is approaching. More Than a Hundred Prominent Figures Initiate a Public Memorial Service for Xu Yutang

January 3rd at the Buddhist Pure Land Society

Wang Xia, Xiong Xiling, Zhu Chenlan, Wu Tiecheng, Ye Gongchuo, Zheng Hongnian, and 126 others jointly initiated a public memorial service for Mr. Xu Yutang, the grandfather of Mr. Xu Jingren, on January 3rd next year. The invitation distributed yesterday stated: "Respectfully informing you, Taiqiu's virtue moved 30,000 mourners, and the esteemed elder lived in seclusion until the age of 104. Moreover, he belonged to the prestigious Ruying clan and was deservedly recognized as the blessed star of Anhui. Like Mr. Xu Jingren's grandfather, Mr. Yutang, in Qiupu, his hidden virtue remained fragrant, and his spirit did not fade away. He built nests in the misty caves, his beauty rivaling that of Shen Liao. He rectified customs in front of the Zhongxin Hall, his teachings bequeathing stability. Zhang Cun showed filial piety, scattered silken brocades. Zeng Gong was kind and gentle, caring for his four younger brothers and nine younger sisters. He was granted the honor of being presented with a walking stick, no different from the elders of the Lu Kingdom. He had the vision to eat coarse rice, no less than the sincerity of Zhongxuan. Heaven ended his spiritual journey, becoming a guest in the Tushita Heaven. The world commonly praised him as someone from whom teachings could be requested, as someone destined for the Buddhist realm. We await the auspicious events. Zhao Duanming had great writings, even more admirable than the three generations of the Jin Tangs, with many virtuous descendants like Han Wei'gong. Mr. Jingren, following the earnest instructions of his will, avoided the common rituals of the floating world. He trained himself to be thrifty and determined to be cautious to the end. We have long admired his virtues and share in the sorrow. Therefore, we have decided to set up a public memorial service at the Buddhist Pure Land Society on Hede Road in Shanghai on January 3, 1933, which is the eighth day of the twelfth lunar month of the Ren Shen year. We will piously recite the true scriptures, hoping for his rebirth in the Buddhist realm and looking forward to the destruction of the main tomb in Teng Lu. We will be respectful and sincere in our offerings, reverently paying homage to the spirits of the tall mountains and lofty peaks. We dare to prepare a dignified burial and respectfully await the arrival of vehicles and horses, using elegies to forever express our sorrow. We respectfully inform you and offer our regards. We hope you will consider. Counterfeiting of National Goods by Imitating Chinese Cloth Trademarks

Wujin Dyeing and Weaving Guild

Sends Personnel to Shanghai for Investigation

The Guowen News Agency reports that the National General Chamber of Commerce sent a letter yesterday to the Shanghai Municipal Government and the Bureau of Social Affairs, stating: "We are writing to you regarding a letter received from the Wujin County Chamber of Commerce in Jiangsu. The letter from Xu Hankang, Chairman of the Standing Committee of the local Dyeing and Weaving Industry Guild, states that the products of our guild are sold to various provinces and are shipped through Shanghai. Since the boycott of foreign goods, Japanese merchants, seeing the popularity of domestic goods, have colluded with unscrupulous merchants to counterfeit national goods trademarks. This has been discovered repeatedly and has even been the subject of lawsuits. If this continues, it will not only affect the future of national goods, but also render the boycott efforts futile. After repeated discussions, our guild members agreed that it is difficult to investigate these matters from a distance. Therefore, it is necessary to establish an office in Shanghai for the Wujin Dyeing and Weaving Factories to send personnel to investigate. If counterfeiting of trademarks is discovered, we can report it to the authorities for investigation and handling at any time. We are writing to your association to request your review and to inform the county government to forward the information to the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs for record. We are also writing to the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce to request them to forward the information to various agencies for their attention."

"In view of the fact that the counterfeiting of trademarks of cloth manufacturers in our county has occurred frequently and has been reported in the past, and that the guild considers it necessary to establish an office in Shanghai for the purpose of preventing such abuses, promoting the sale of domestic products, and facilitating investigation, we are submitting this letter to your association. We request that you forward it to the Municipal Government and Bureau to protect national goods and prevent counterfeiting. We value our public relationship."

"We are therefore writing to your government and bureau, requesting your attention to this matter."

A Record of the Regular Meeting of the Shanghai Branch of the Association of Chinese Engineers

The Shanghai Branch of the Association of Chinese Engineers held its regular meeting at 6 p.m. on the 28th of last month at the Bank Association at No. 4 Hong Kong Road. Forty-eight people attended, including Mr. Wang Shengzu. They first had a dinner, and then the president, Mr. Xu Peihuang, reported on the election of this branch. Following this, Mr. Qiu Lin (transliteration), manager of the Victory Company, gave a lecture on the method of manufacturing gramophone records. Mr. Qiu also brought the company's gramophone and recording machine for a demonstration. The sound was very clear and pleasant, and the lecture was very detailed, providing valuable information for engineers.

President Xu then proposed that, as the association has many members, it is difficult for new and old members to get to know each other. Even after introductions at branch meetings, they often do not know each other's names, which is not ideal. To remedy this, he proposed making name badges to be distributed to members at the next meeting to help them recognize each other. The members present unanimously agreed, and Mr. Dong Dagang is actively drawing up a design. The meeting adjourned after ten o'clock.

Circular from the Mechanical Industry Association to its Members

Abolishing Previously Issued Certificates of National Goods

And Establishing Provisional Transportation Certificates

A letter from the Shanghai Mechanical National Goods Factories Association to its member factories states: "Regarding the certificates of national goods that our association has been issuing, since the September 18th Incident, the call to resist Japan and save the nation has grown. Member factories have requested certificates for proof, but there have been irregularities. These national goods certificates are permanent, and if we are not careful, they may be used by unscrupulous merchants for fraudulent purposes, which would greatly affect the interests of our members. The Standing Committee of our association has considered this and decided to invalidate all existing national goods certificates. In the future, members who need certification for transporting national goods can obtain provisional certificates from the association by submitting an application. This will ensure proper management."

"In addition to announcing the invalidation of the certificates in the newspaper, we are enclosing a blank application form for your information."

The Ningbo Fellow-Villagers Association Sends a Letter Requesting Protection of Chen Song's Property Rights

Where the Floodwaters Reach is All Sandy Land; Without Property Protection, the People Cannot Live in Peace

The Old Ningbo Shatian Sub-Bureau's handling of the Shatian reclamation project is not following the proper procedures. Land that matured hundreds of years ago and has been managed by the people for a long time is being included in the reclamation area. Land with legal deeds and registration certificates is being sold off without proper notification, citing overdue registration and payment. The number of such cases is unknown, and the public is in an uproar. It is reported that the Ningbo Fellow-Villagers Association in Shanghai sent a letter to the Yin County government yesterday regarding the illegal handling of Chen Song's property by the sub-bureau, stating: "Mr. Chen Yeqiao, a member of our association, owns 5.38 mu of land (according to the Shatian Sub-Bureau's re-measurement, it is 5.12 mu) in the name of Chen Songfang, located in Dongba No. 8 Tu of Yin County. He has built a house on it and lived there for more than ten years, holding a stamped deed and having registered it with the Ningbo Municipal Government Land Bureau. Last November, the house was unfortunately destroyed by fire, and Mr. Chen and his family temporarily moved elsewhere, losing touch with the land. Unexpectedly, in September of this year, the land was reportedly auctioned off by the Shatian Sub-Bureau for over 400 yuan. Mr. Chen entrusted our association to find a way to request the county magistrate to instruct the Shatian Sub-Bureau to withdraw the auction and protect his property rights. Now, Mr. Chen claims that the land has been managed and housed for many years and is completely different from sandy mudflats. The Shatian Sub-Bureau has refused the original owner's request for restoration, citing overdue payment, which is an unfair act. On November 25th, they posted a notice at the door of Chen Songfang's house allowing Zhang Lingrong, a representative of Song Ji, to demarcate the land for management, which is alarming. If this kind of action by the Shatian Sub-Bureau is not corrected, then where the floodwaters reach is all sandy land. The people cannot live in peace without property protection. This is probably not the government's original intention in reclaiming the Shatian."

"Therefore, we earnestly request that you investigate and provide legal relief to protect property rights."

Rev. Yu Zongzhou Memorial Service

Organized by Xie Yongqin

"Since Christianity was introduced to China over a century ago, its influence and number of followers have been widely recognized. However, church affairs have always relied on foreign influence and unequal treaties to preach in the interior and establish a foundation. This has aroused the resentment of the Chinese people. In the 32nd year of the Guangxu reign of the Qing Dynasty, Yu Zongzhou, a pastor of the Presbyterian Church, from Ningbo, Zhejiang, believed that Christianity should be shared by all mankind and that China could accept it. However, it was unacceptable to use unequal treaties to protect the church. Therefore, he and his comrades Chai Lianfu, Chen Ao, Lin Hongbin, Zhu Baoluo, Xie Yongqin, Lin Meichuan, Fan Zhidu, Zhu Lianqing, and Pang Zixian organized the National General Association of the Jesus Self-Supporting Church in Shanghai. They established over 300 branches in provinces, cities, counties, and overseas Chinese communities to achieve the long-held goal of self-propagation, self-support, and self-governance. Christian groups in other provinces followed suit and broke away from Western influence to realize an indigenous Chinese church. Mr. Yu's contribution is truly significant."

"Although Mr. Yu was 80 years old this year, he was still in good spirits and had much to contribute. However, he fell ill on the 15th of last month and passed away the next morning. The news shocked the nation. His family held a funeral at the International Funeral Home on the 26th of the same month and temporarily placed his coffin in the Siming Guild Hall, as reported in the previous newspaper. It is now reported that the association, in recognition of Mr. Yu's service to the church, his efforts in self-reliance, and his hard work, which benefited the world, and his dedication to social causes, has decided to hold a memorial service on January 8th of next year to express their condolences. Mr. Xie Yongqin has been appointed as the chairman of the preparatory committee to oversee all preparations. The association stated that anyone who admires Mr. Yu's life and wishes to express their respect should send condolences and elegies to the association's office at No. 117 Sida Lane, Shikuta Road, North Sichuan Road, Shanghai, by the end of December so that they can be published in a special memorial issue."

The Notorious Bandit Did Not Commit Crimes in Shanghai

But Committed Kidnapping and Murder in Shaoxing

Awaiting the Zhejiang Security Team to Bring Documents to Shanghai for Extradition

Hua Detective Su Changsheng and Detective Zhou Guisen of the Laozha Police Station previously arrested the notorious bandit Chen Zhaoyuan (also known as Ni Si) from Shaoxing, along with Yuan Guanggeng, Yuan Diancai, Ma Zhengcai, Lu Zhenggong, and women Chen Hu, Yuan Wang, Chen Sanfeng, and Jin Wang, at Dongyouheng Road. They confiscated a pistol with fifty rounds of ammunition and over 8,000 yuan. They were handed over to the First Special District Court for interrogation and detention. The police have now found that Chen and the other criminals committed major crimes such as kidnapping for ransom and murder in Shaoxing. They did not commit any crimes in this city. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Special Court. The police lawyer, Ru Baoyi, stated that the Zhejiang Provincial Government Security Team has requested the extradition of the criminals in this case. The female criminals do not need to be extradited. Members of the Security Team have returned to the province to prepare documents and will arrive in Shanghai in one or two days. He requested that the case be postponed, that the female criminals be released first, and that the remaining criminals be detained. The presiding judge approved the request and ordered the four female criminals, including Hu Chen, to be released first. Chen Zhaoqi and the other five were returned to custody for further interrogation at a later date.

Only Son Dies Tragically

Yesterday morning at around 10:30 a.m., Wang Xing, the owner of the Jiuchang Ironworks in Zhuangyuanda Lane, Hongkou, whose native place is Ningbo, had an only son named Yiwen, who was two years old. An apprentice, Zhu Shichang (13 years old), took him to play in the middle of the road. A horse-drawn carriage No. 180 from the Ma Carriage Company on Ti'an Bridge Maohai Road came speeding along. They were unable to avoid it in time, and the two children were knocked to the ground. Zhu's head and legs were injured, and Yiwen's skull was crushed. He was dying. A patrol officer arrived and took the injured children to Tongren Hospital. Because Yiwen's injuries were too severe, he was transferred to Guangren Hospital, where he died.

Electrical Manufacturing Industry Organizes Guild

Initiated by Hu Xiyuan and Others

Approved by the Municipal Party Headquarters

There are dozens of factories in Shanghai that manufacture electrical appliances. There has been no contact or organization among the businesses. Therefore, when foreign goods are dumped and attacked, they are often unable to resist because they are not united and are defeated one by one. Now, Hu Xiyuan and others in the industry have initiated the organization of a trade association. In September, they submitted a request to the Municipal Party Headquarters for registration. Due to the central government's revision of various laws and regulations, approval was delayed. Now, Hu Xiyuan and others have received a reply from the Municipal Party Headquarters, which reads: "Reply No. 189 of the Chinese Kuomintang Committee: Reply to the request of Hu Xiyuan and others to organize the Shanghai Electrical Manufacturing Industry Trade Association, with attached resumes. Having examined the submitted documents, the request is approved for registration, and a permit will be issued. Please send a representative to the headquarters to collect the permit." It is reported that the initiators have already collected the permit and are starting to prepare for the organization of the guild.
