Novel

Written to a Friend's Wife (Continued 1)

— Qin Shouou

Because all three of my younger brothers are half-siblings, we have absolutely no feelings for each other. We are worse than neighbors. Therefore, since I was young, I have had an unusual inclination towards classmates who had similar tastes, as a kind of consolation to replace "brotherly love." Zhou Dajing was also considered to have similar tastes.

The day before I left my hometown, Lin Baocheng 丨 also a classmate 丨 told me that Zhou Dajing had married a very beautiful and lively wife, and that she would be coming to Shanghai with him this time; however, he did not tell me your name at that time. To be honest, when I heard it, I didn't pay special attention to it, just like after reading a bland news item in the newspaper, leaving a very faint shadow in my mind.

"I never thought that Zhou Dajing, who had lost his youthful vitality due to the sorrow of unrequited love, would marry someone quietly; and marry a very beautiful and lively wife. How unexpected!" On the evening of the day I arrived in Shanghai, I decided to go to Seward Road to visit your new home. After the tram passed Dent Road, in my complex and chaotic mind, there was suddenly a thought focused on curiosity, rushing very quickly.

At that time, the house you lived in was truly elegant and beautiful. Short and dense shrubs were arranged like guards on the sidewalk in front of the gate. Although there were no colorful flowers in the middle, there was only a touch of deep green, but it looked even more beautiful and clean. In fact, a house like this is not worthy to house an angel like you! I often thought like that later.

When the sound of my patent leather shoes hitting the stone steps was very crisp, a short window with green gauze curtains was immediately opened. A man's head poked out. 丨 A very strange one.

The smooth and tidy long hair had been cut into a buzz cut as short as peach fuzz; the slightly yellow face seemed to have turned dark black from the long-term fumigation of gas; and a pair of deep-lensed glasses that he didn't have before had been added to his nose. Zhou Dajing had simply died once and been reborn!

"Who are you looking for?" Of course, I didn't recognize him, and he didn't see clearly that it was me. Like a sentinel during martial law, asking a pedestrian for a "password," I unexpectedly received this stern question from him.

The form can be changed as much as possible, but the voice always remains the same; thanks to him opening his mouth like this, I knew it was him. At the same time, a copper sign that was not very noticeable on the door, "Lawyer Zhou Dajing," suddenly caught my eye.

Of course, the words "lawyer" were not enough to surprise me: besides, at that time, I was still a normal friend with integrity, and there was no need to be surprised.

"I am Zhu Jinchi, a born communist." 丨 After I announced my name with a humorous tone, that Zhou Da lawyer of yours, who took marriage as revenge for losing his job, quickly opened the door and welcomed me out.

"Jinchi, it's you! Come in! Come in!" His warm and sincere welcome made me feel the joy of reuniting with an old friend. At that time, I almost wanted to hug him and kiss him!

Then, naturally, it was the scene of "Suddenly Meeting That Charming Nemesis." Dear little friend, you probably haven't forgotten it, have you?

Under the humorous, sweet, and quiet green light emitted by the light green light bulb, you, indescribably beautiful, were standing generously beside a purple-red embroidered curtain wearing a light green spring dress. The alluring smile, the flowing eyes, the beautiful contours; everything, everything, was as fast and powerful as the bullets fired by the Japanese Type 38 automatic rifle, directly hitting the depths of my heart.

Ah! God! Just in that moment of three or four seconds, my life's destiny was determined 丨 That was the thirteenth, and it was Friday, truly the most unfavorable day. The many sorrows, worries, struggles, and insomnia that I suffered afterward, and even today's escape, are all gifts given to me by this unfavorable day!

But I don't hate it at all, and I even want to thank it! Because I have already taken your bright red and warm heart from the opportunity it has given me. 丨 At least half of it, that's what I can guarantee myself!

Movie Special

International News

The Special Characteristics of the Soviet Film Industry

— Ms. Wen Yin

The Soviet film industry has two distinct characteristics that distinguish it from the film industries of other countries: 1.

The Soviet film industry is state-run. From writing scripts, training actors, shooting films to distribution and screening, everything is completely under the control of the state. 2. The Soviet film industry is not a commercial, profit-making business, but a broad-based educational activity for culture and art.

At the beginning of the revolution, Soviet revolutionary leaders had long recognized the great significance of film in education and art. In order to strengthen the educational role of film, a decision was made that the content of all films must be reviewed by the People's Commissariat for Education and the government's propaganda department. The content of every film takes as its premise the education of the broad masses of workers and peasants, and guiding them to advance towards a new society. The government uses film to instill general and political education to the public, and to conduct extensive propaganda about the new society and its ideology. In the period when the culture of Tsarist Russia had been abandoned and the new Russian culture was continuing to grow, the role of film in the formation of mass art was particularly important and great. Completely reversing the traditional view of film as a pastime and entertainment, the Soviet Union uniquely recognized film as the art of the mechanical age, and further recognized it as the art of the masses, using it as a driving force for shaping the mass culture of the new society.

Because the Soviet authorities recognized the true value and function of film in education and art, the decision was made to nationalize the film industry. The Soviet law on nationalizing the film industry was signed by Lenin on August 27, 1919, and promulgated by the People's Committee. Before this, in February 1918, when the revolutionary government was first established, the Soviet People's Commissariat for Education had already established film specialized committees in Leningrad and Moscow to plan the film industry at that time. Since the promulgation of the nationalization law, the Soviet film industry has undergone a distinctly different change in direction from before, and its attitude of fighting for mass culture and mass art has become even more clear and resolute. The special development of the Soviet film industry in recent years is rooted in this. This is not only a milestone achievement in the Soviet film industry, but also a new era in the world film industry. (This article is taken from the Soviet Yearbook)

Film Review

The Big Broadcast

— Yan Nan

Half of Paramount's "Top Ten Special Blockbusters" for this year have already been moved to the screens in Shanghai. "The Big Broadcast," one tenth of the set, has been hailed as the best of the ten films by the American media. 丨 From my personal point of view, I also extremely sympathize with this view.

It is very similar to "Broadway Melody" and "The Great Gabbo", but it is much more interesting and powerful. The United States has been much more deserted for this kind of all-song film. After "Paramount on Parade," we can no longer see Paramount have this kind of film; 丨 There is 丨 This one. However, it is very obvious that this time there is an amazing progress.

It is not similar to any other musical; it has a complex plot, a huge amount of songs, and it tries its best to compress a very long story; and the second half is completely focused on songs. The wonder of the whole film lies in those songs; there are love songs, jazz songs, tragic Classic, and black folk songs. All of them have unique situational music, and sometimes some tap dance is interspersed, 丨丨 But the beauty of this kind of song and dance can never be described in words!

At the beginning, it takes a radio station as the center; the result is still there, adding a comedy of two pairs of lovers reuniting at the end. The narration in the first half makes the most of the wonderful parts of the plot, and the three actors also perform seamlessly! Even without song and dance, it can be called a "passionate masterpiece." The actors are all newcomers to the screen, but they will use ingenious methods to tell us everyone's names. The song and dance in the last section also adds the manager's few static performances, so that the whole film does not deviate from the topic. The photography and set design are all very artistic.…… In short, this director is really more superb than Lubitsch and DeMille.

If you usually like to watch movies, or are quite interested in American radio songs: then you would rather sacrifice any one thousand films, or even sell your radio, you should watch this unparalleled masterpiece!

Movie Star Biography

Tianyi Music Director Ma Loufen

— Xiao Ma

Tianyi's Xiaosheng [young male lead] Ma Loufen is from Wuxian, Jiangsu Province; he grew up in Shanghai since he was a child. At the age of fifteen, he entered the attached middle school of Guanghua University. He usually liked to learn music. If there was a recreational party in the school, Ma Jun would enthusiastically participate in the performance; the students and teachers in the school praised him very much. After graduation, at the age of seventeen, he entered the Chinese Song and Dance Troupe founded by the modern songwriter Li Jinhui as a music teacher. His performances in Shanghai were able to win social praise.

Later, he followed Li to perform in the Nanyang Islands and other places, and was also praised by the local people; when he returned to China, he was eighteen years old.

After leaving Li's Chinese Song and Dance Troupe, he founded the Tianma Song and Dance Troupe himself; he performed in the Xiamen area, and then joined the Jimei Song and Dance Troupe run by Wang Tiyu, and traveled all over the Shanghai-Ningbo area. He was so confused for three years. Later, he was introduced by Li to Tianyi Film Company. Shao Zuiweng, the old owner of Tianyi, valued him very much, and invited him and Chen Yumei to co-star in a sound film "Girl Yunlan"; the results were not bad. Mr. Ma is now only twenty-three years old.

Talk about domestic films

(I) After Seeing "Three Modern Women"

— Ling He

Lianhua's "Three Modern Women" was previewed at the New Light Theater the day before yesterday. I had the accidental opportunity to appreciate it.

"This is a film worth seeing," I will say at the outset. The film's structure is as follows: it is still a love story, in which three modern women of different classes simultaneously fall in love with one man. One is a socialite from high society; one is a woman from the middle class who is a lover of individualism; one is a telephone operator from a petit bourgeois background.

The story is quite perfectly interwoven, with twists and turns, but also with elements of "contrivance". Director Bu Wancang has made progress both in terms of consciousness and technique.

In terms of acting technique, it can be said that several important roles were quite successful, especially Ruan Lingyu; I admit that she has a special kind of intelligence.

Chen Yanyan is exactly that innocent, that pure. Li Zhuozhuo can also represent that kind of typical character. Jin Yan still maintains his usual achievements.

There are several good scenes, such as the realistic depiction of the coolies on the Bund. The dance scene lacked sophistication. Zhou Shuzhen's flying kiss ruined part of the plot. Chen Ruoying's suicide was too ordinary. The subtitles were imperfect, but some had literary meaning.

Finally, my conclusion is this: this is a successful work by Bu Wancang, although there are still some mistakes in it, but "everyone makes mistakes. As long as I can fully overcome these mistakes," I would like to present these lines of dialogue (from the subtitles) to Mr. Bu.

(II) After Seeing "Little Actress"

— Yi Lie

There are several sections that seem to lack authenticity and naturalness. Although there are distorted facts in a distorted modern society, the descriptions are somewhat exaggerated.

Ji Zhong's wife, Wang, and her lover, Chen Naixin, arrange a rendezvous by telephone, preparing to elope. Ji Zhong becomes ill with anger, moaning in bed, thirstily calling for water. His wife, Wang, not only does not give him water, but also complains loudly, unable to hear the telephone. Later, carrying her suitcase, she leaves. Afterwards, the same thing happens to Wang. Chen Naixin treats Wang in the same way that Wang treated her husband. This contrast, although exciting for the audience, inevitably has the ridiculousness of "play-acting" in terms of reality.

Chen Naixin goes to Wang's bedroom, and is seen by Xiao Lin, who tells her uncle and asks him why he doesn't get along with his aunt. Her aunt is friendly with other men; isn't her uncle angry? One is mediocre and muddled, one is smart and lively; the performances are vivid and thorough.

Yuan Meiyun, who plays Xiao Lin, truly has acting talent; although she is new to the camera, she doesn't seem inexperienced.

(III) Some Opinions on "Struggle"

— Qi Xi

The play "Struggle" certainly has "struggle," but unfortunately it cannot "struggle" to the end. Xiao Zheng joins the volunteer army and participates in the battle. If this war is about the Battle of Shanghai, then we failed in the Battle of Shanghai. Therefore, I would rather Xiao Zheng die in battle than have him return alive. If this war is about the Battle of the Black Water and White Mountains, then it is not yet time to return. Struggle means struggling to the end, but what does "Struggle" give us?

In the last two scenes, what is implied to us is: Xiao Zheng is wearing the uniform of the volunteer army, embracing his person - Yan Gu... Xiao Zheng has changed into a suit, and is boating with his lover. These facts tell us: Xiao Zheng's struggle for the country was not thorough; at the same time, his struggle for love was successful. This is the final result of my seeing "Struggle".

Minor Opinions

Exploration of Film Publications

— Xin Mo

For film fans, film publications are, of course, the most cherished reading material.

I guess a film fan doesn't have that much time to collect and read all the film publications! Perhaps there are such people, but most likely they only select one or two of the better ones!

Many people always start things but never finish them. Take film publications, for example. When some were first published, they were very satisfying to readers. This was not only a feast for the eyes of film fans, but also provided guidance in the film industry. Later, the content not only became less substantial, but also many worthless articles were published. Recently, several publications have made this mistake, filling the pages with trivial matters about female stars. If film publications are only about recording trivial matters about female stars, they will fundamentally become uninteresting publications.

Therefore, I hope that the gentlemen who edit film publications will not fail in their important mission.

The Editor

Film Treatise

Comparing the Studio to "The Land of Illusion"

— Chen Dabe

This laughing exercise method is very related to your health. If you are determined to continue working hard in the art of performance, if you are determined to build your career in the studio, you will have to endure a lot of pain in the future, both psychologically and physically, pain that you would never taste in other professions.

Friends who have never experienced studio life only glimpse the bright side of the studio from the screen, and think that studio life is a kind of fun and ideal life. Some people see many brilliant stars, and even compare the studio to "The Land of Illusion." This is completely wrong.

The male and female staff actors in the studio are made of flesh and blood, just like the men and women you encounter in other groups. In other groups, you feel that the number of "petty people" is greater than the number of "gentlemen." It is the same in the studio. In school life, new students are often bullied by older students. When you are an extra or play a minor role in the studio, the bullying you suffer is probably even more than when you are a new student. Arrogant airs, sarcastic criticisms, and even rude rebukes and barbaric scoldings, in today's Chinese studios, can almost everywhere make a newcomer feel uneasy, and almost the same situation as a daughter-in-law in front of her evil mother-in-law.

As for working hours? In the studio, no matter in which country, there are no so-called legal hours. In those small companies that rely on the sun, you are busy from morning to night, and even eating becomes a problem. In those large companies that rely on electric light, your working hours can be extended until after dawn. When you see your blacklisted colleagues full of excitement, you are already so tired that your back hurts, and you just want to lie down.
